The mists had no more than partially dissolved,\r\nand all that he could distinguish was a narrow circle of red sand dotted\r\nwith ten or twenty bushes.\r\n\r\nHe felt a soft, cool touch on the back of his neck. He started forward\r\nin nervous fright and, in doing so, tumbled over onto the sand. Looking\r\nup over his shoulder quickly, he was astounded to see a woman standing\r\nbeside him.\r\n\r\nShe was clothed in a single flowing, pale green garment, rather\r\nclassically draped. According to earth standards she was not beautiful,\r\nfor, although her face was otherwise human, she was endowed\xe2\x80\x94or\r\nafflicted\xe2\x80\x94with the additional disfiguring organs that Maskull had\r\ndiscovered in himself. She also possessed the heart tentacle. But when\r\nhe sat up, and their eyes met and remained in sympathetic contact, he\r\nseemed to see right into a soul that was the home of love, warmth,\r\nkindness, tenderness, and intimacy. Such was the noble familiarity of\r\nthat gaze, that he thought he knew her. After that, he recognised all\r\nthe loveliness of her person. She was tall and slight. All her movements\r\nwere as graceful as music. Her skin was not of a dead, opaque colour,\r\nlike that of an earth beauty, but was opalescent; its hue was\r\ncontinually changing, with every thought and emotion, but none of these\r\ntints was vivid\xe2\x80\x94all were delicate, half-toned, and poetic. She had very\r\nlong, loosely plaited, flaxen hair. The new organs, as soon as Maskull\r\nhad familiarised himself with them, imparted something to her face that\r\nwas unique and striking. He could not quite define it to himself, but\r\nsubtlety and inwardness seemed added. The organs did not contradict the\r\nlove of her eyes or the angelic purity of her features, but nevertheless\r\nsounded a deeper note\xe2\x80\x94a note that saved her from mere girlishness.\r\n\r\nHer gaze was so friendly and unembarrassed that Maskull felt scarcely\r\nany humiliation at sitting at her feet, naked and helpless. She realised\r\nhis plight, and put into his hands a garment that she had been carrying\r\nover her arm. It was similar to the one she was wearing, but of a\r\ndarker, more masculine colour.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you think you can put it on by yourself?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe was distinctly conscious of these words, yet her voice had not\r\nsounded.\r\n\r\nHe forced himself up to his feet, and she helped him to master the\r\ncomplications of the drapery.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPoor man\xe2\x80\x94how you are suffering!\xe2\x80\x9d she said, in the same inaudible\r\nlanguage. This time he discovered that the sense of what she said was\r\nreceived by his brain through the organ on his forehead.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere am I? Is this Tormance?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked. As he spoke, he staggered.\r\n\r\nShe caught him, and helped him to sit down. \xe2\x80\x9cYes. You are with friends.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThen she regarded him with a smile, and began speaking aloud, in\r\nEnglish. Her voice somehow reminded him of an April day, it was so\r\nfresh, nervous, and girlish. \xe2\x80\x9cI can now understand your language. It was\r\nstrange at first. In the future I\xe2\x80\x99ll speak to you with my mouth.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is extraordinary! What is this organ?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked, touching his\r\nforehead.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is named the \xe2\x80\x98breve.\xe2\x80\x99 By means of it we read one another\xe2\x80\x99s thoughts.\r\nStill, speech is better, for then the heart can be read too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cThey say that speech is given us to deceive others.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne can deceive with thought, too. But I\xe2\x80\x99m thinking of the best, not\r\nthe worst.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you seen my friends?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe scrutinised him quietly, before answering. \xe2\x80\x9cDid you not come alone?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI came with two other men, in a machine. I must have lost consciousness\r\non arrival, and I haven\xe2\x80\x99t seen them since.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s very strange! No, I haven\xe2\x80\x99t seen them. They can\xe2\x80\x99t be here, or we\r\nwould have known it. My husband and I\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is your name, and your husband\xe2\x80\x99s name?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMine is Joiwind\xe2\x80\x94my husband\xe2\x80\x99s is Panawe. We live a very long way from\r\nhere; still, it came to us both last night that you were lying here\r\ninsensible. We almost quarrelled about which of us should come to you,\r\nbut in the end I won.\xe2\x80\x9d Here she laughed. \xe2\x80\x9cI won, because I am the\r\nstronger-hearted of the two; he is the purer in perception.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThanks, Joiwind!\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull simply.\r\n\r\nThe colors chased each other rapidly beneath her skin. \xe2\x80\x9cOh, why do you\r\nsay that? What pleasure is greater than loving-kindness? I rejoiced at\r\nthe opportunity.... But now we must exchange blood.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is this?\xe2\x80\x9d he demanded, rather puzzled.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt must be so. Your blood is far too thick and heavy for our world.\r\nUntil you have an infusion of mine, you will never get up.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull flushed. \xe2\x80\x9cI feel like a complete ignoramus here.... Won\xe2\x80\x99t it\r\nhurt you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf your blood pains you, I suppose it will pain me. But we will share\r\nthe pain.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is a new kind of hospitality to me,\xe2\x80\x9d he muttered.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWouldn\xe2\x80\x99t you do the same for me?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Joiwind, half smiling, half\r\nagitated.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t answer for any of my actions in this world. I scarcely know\r\nwhere I am.... Why, yes\xe2\x80\x94of course I would, Joiwind.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhile they were talking it had become full day. The mists had rolled\r\naway from the ground, and only the upper atmosphere remained fog-\r\ncharged. The desert of scarlet sand stretched in all directions, except\r\none, where there was a sort of little oasis\xe2\x80\x94some low hills, clothed\r\nsparsely with little purple trees from base to summit. It was about a\r\nquarter of a mile distant.\r\n\r\nJoiwind had brought with her a small flint knife. Without any trace of\r\nnervousness, she made a careful, deep incision on her upper arm. Maskull\r\nexpostulated.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally, this part of it is nothing,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, laughing. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd if it\r\nwere\xe2\x80\x94a sacrifice that is no sacrifice\xe2\x80\x94what merit is there in that?...\r\nCome now\xe2\x80\x94your arm!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe blood was streaming down her arm. It was not red blood, but a milky,\r\nopalescent fluid.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot that one!\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, shrinking. \xe2\x80\x9cI have already been cut\r\nthere.\xe2\x80\x9d He submitted the other, and his blood poured forth.\r\n\r\nJoiwind delicately and skilfully placed the mouths of the two wounds\r\ntogether, and then kept her arm pressed tightly against Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s for a\r\nlong time. He felt a stream of pleasure entering his body through the\r\nincision. His old lightness and vigour began to return to him. After\r\nabout five minutes a duel of kindness started between them; he wanted to\r\nremove his arm, and she to continue. At last he had his way, but it was\r\nnone too soon\xe2\x80\x94she stood there pale and dispirited.\r\n\r\nShe looked at him with a more serious expression than before, as if\r\nstrange depths had opened up before her eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is your name?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMaskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere have you come from, with this awful blood?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom a world called Earth.... The blood is clearly unsuitable for this\r\nworld, Joiwind, but after all, that was only to be expected. I am sorry\r\nI let you have your way.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, don\xe2\x80\x99t say that! There was nothing else to be done. We must all help\r\none another. Yet, somehow\xe2\x80\x94forgive me\xe2\x80\x94I feel polluted.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd well you may, for it\xe2\x80\x99s a fearful thing for a girl to accept in her\r\nown veins the blood of a strange man from a strange planet. If I had not\r\nbeen so dazed and weak I would never have allowed it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut I would have insisted. Are we not all brothers and sisters? Why did\r\nyou come here, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe was conscious of a slight degree of embarrassment. \xe2\x80\x9cWill you think it\r\nfoolish if I say I hardly know?\xe2\x80\x94I came with those two men. Perhaps I was\r\nattracted by curiosity, or perhaps it was the love of adventure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps,\xe2\x80\x9d said Joiwind. \xe2\x80\x9cI wonder... These friends of yours must be\r\nterrible men. Why did they come?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat I can tell you. They came to follow Surtur.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer face grew troubled. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t understand it. One of them at least\r\nmust be a bad man, and yet if he is following Surtur\xe2\x80\x94or Shaping, as he\r\nis called here\xe2\x80\x94he can\xe2\x80\x99t be really bad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you know of Surtur?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull in astonishment.\r\n\r\nJoiwind remained silent for a time, studying his face. His brain moved\r\nrestlessly, as though it were being probed from outside. \xe2\x80\x9cI see.... and\r\nyet I don\xe2\x80\x99t see,\xe2\x80\x9d she said at last. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is very difficult.... Your God\r\nis a dreadful Being\xe2\x80\x94bodyless, unfriendly, invisible. Here we don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nworship a God like that. Tell me, has any man set eyes on your God?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat does all this mean, Joiwind? Why speak of God?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI want to know.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn ancient times, when the earth was young and grand, a few holy men\r\nare reputed to have walked and spoken with God, but those days are\r\npast.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOur world is still young,\xe2\x80\x9d said Joiwind. \xe2\x80\x9cShaping goes among us and\r\nconverses with us. He is real and active\xe2\x80\x94a friend and lover. Shaping\r\nmade us, and he loves his work.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you met him?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded Maskull, hardly believing his ears.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo. I have done nothing to deserve it yet. Some day I may have an\r\nopportunity to sacrifice myself, and then I may be rewarded by meeting\r\nand talking with Shaping.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have certainly come to another world. We women call him Shaping, and so do most men, but\r\na few name him Surtur.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull bit his nail. \xe2\x80\x9cHave you ever heard of Crystalman?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is Shaping once again. You see, he has many names\xe2\x80\x94which shows how\r\nmuch he occupies our minds. Crystalman is a name of affection.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s odd,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cI came here with quite different ideas about\r\nCrystalman.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nJoiwind shook her hair. \xe2\x80\x9cIn that grove of trees over there stands a\r\ndesert shrine of his. Let us go and pray there, and then we\xe2\x80\x99ll go on our\r\nway to Poolingdred. That is my home. It\xe2\x80\x99s a long way off, and we must\r\nget there before Blodsombre.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow, what is Blodsombre?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor about four hours in the middle of the day Branchspell\xe2\x80\x99s rays are so\r\nhot that no one can endure them. We call it Blodsombre.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs Branchspell another name for Arcturus?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nJoiwind threw off her seriousness and laughed. \xe2\x80\x9cNaturally we don\xe2\x80\x99t take\r\nour names from you, Maskull. I don\xe2\x80\x99t think our names are very poetic,\r\nbut they follow nature.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe took his arm affectionately, and directed their walk towards the\r\ntree-covered hills. As they went along, the sun broke through the upper\r\nmists and a terrible gust of scorching heat, like a blast from a\r\nfurnace, struck Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s head. He involuntarily looked up, but lowered\r\nhis eyes again like lightning. All that he saw in that instant was a\r\nglaring ball of electric white, three times the apparent diameter of the\r\nsun. For a few minutes he was quite blind.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy God!\xe2\x80\x9d he exclaimed. \xe2\x80\x9cIf it\xe2\x80\x99s like this in early morning you must be\r\nright enough about Blodsombre.\xe2\x80\x9d When he had somewhat recovered himself\r\nhe asked, \xe2\x80\x9cHow long are the days here, Joiwind?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAgain he felt his brain being probed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt this time of the year, for every hour\xe2\x80\x99s daylight that you have in\r\nsummer, we have two.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe heat is terrific\xe2\x80\x94and yet somehow I don\xe2\x80\x99t feel so distressed by it\r\nas I would have expected.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI feel it more than usual. It\xe2\x80\x99s not difficult to account for it; you\r\nhave some of my blood, and I have some of yours.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, every time I realise that, I\xe2\x80\x94Tell me, Joiwind, will my blood\r\nalter, if I stay here long enough?\xe2\x80\x94I mean, will it lose its redness and\r\nthickness, and become pure and thin and light-coloured, like yours?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy not? If you live as we live, you will assuredly grow like us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you mean food and drink?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe eat no food, and drink only water.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd on that you manage to sustain life?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, Maskull, our water is good water,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Joiwind, smiling.\r\n\r\nAs soon as he could see again he stared around at the landscape. The\r\nenormous scarlet desert extended everywhere to the horizon, excepting\r\nwhere it was broken by the oasis. It was roofed by a cloudless, deep\r\nblue, almost violet, sky. The circle of the horizon was far larger than\r\non earth. On the skyline, at right angles to the direction in which they\r\nwere walking, appeared a chain of mountains, apparently about forty\r\nmiles distant. One, which was higher than the rest, was shaped like a\r\ncup. Maskull would have felt inclined to believe he was travelling in\r\ndreamland, but for the intensity of the light, which made everything\r\nvividly real.\r\n\r\nJoiwind pointed to the cup-shaped mountain. \xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s Poolingdred.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou didn\xe2\x80\x99t come from there!\xe2\x80\x9d he exclaimed, quite startled.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I did indeed. And that is where we have to go to now.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWith the single object of finding me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, yes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe colour mounted to his face. \xe2\x80\x9cThen you are the bravest and noblest of\r\nall girls,\xe2\x80\x9d he said quietly, after a pause. \xe2\x80\x9cWithout exception. Why,\r\nthis is a journey for an athlete!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe pressed his arm, while a score of unpaintable, delicate hues stained\r\nher cheeks in rapid transition. \xe2\x80\x9cPlease don\xe2\x80\x99t say any more about it,\r\nMaskull. It makes me feel unpleasant.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well. But can we possibly get there before midday?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, yes. And you mustn\xe2\x80\x99t be frightened at the distance. We think\r\nnothing of long distances here\xe2\x80\x94we have so much to think about and feel.\r\nTime goes all too quickly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nDuring their conversation they had drawn near the base of the hills,\r\nwhich sloped gently, and were not above fifty feet in height. Maskull\r\nnow began to see strange specimens of vegetable life. What looked like a\r\nsmall patch of purple grass, above five feet square, was moving across\r\nthe sand in their direction. When it came near enough he perceived that\r\nit was not grass; there were no blades, but only purple roots. The roots\r\nwere revolving, for each small plant in the whole patch, like the spokes\r\nof a rimless wheel. They were alternately plunged in the sand, and\r\nwithdrawn from it, and by this means the plant proceeded forward. Some\r\nuncanny, semi-intelligent instinct was keeping all the plants together,\r\nmoving at one pace, in one direction, like a flock of migrating birds in\r\nflight.\r\n\r\nAnother remarkable plant was a large, feathery ball, resembling a\r\ndandelion fruit, which they encountered sailing through the air. Joiwind\r\ncaught it with an exceedingly graceful movement of her arm, and showed\r\nit to Maskull. It had roots and presumably lived in the air and fed on\r\nthe chemical constituents of the atmosphere. But what was peculiar about\r\nit was its colour. It was an entirely new colour\xe2\x80\x94not a new shade or\r\ncombination, but a new primary colour, as vivid as blue, red, or yellow,\r\nbut quite different. When he inquired, she told him that it was known as\r\n\xe2\x80\x9culfire.\xe2\x80\x9d Presently he met with a second new colour. This she designated\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cjale.\xe2\x80\x9d The sense impressions caused in Maskull by these two additional\r\nprimary colors can only be vaguely hinted at by analogy. Just as blue is\r\ndelicate and mysterious, yellow clear and unsubtle, and red sanguine and\r\npassionate, so he felt ulfire to be wild and painful, and jale\r\ndreamlike, feverish, and voluptuous.\r\n\r\nThe hills were composed of a rich, dark mould. Small trees, of weird\r\nshapes, all differing from each other, but all purple-coloured, covered\r\nthe slopes and top. Maskull and Joiwind climbed up and through. Some\r\nhard fruit, bright blue in colour, of the size of a large apple, and\r\nshaped like an egg, was lying in profusion underneath the trees.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs the fruit here poisonous, or why don\xe2\x80\x99t you eat it?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\nShe looked at him tranquilly. \xe2\x80\x9cWe don\xe2\x80\x99t eat living things. The thought\r\nis horrible to us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have nothing to say against that, theoretically. But do you really\r\nsustain your bodies on water?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSupposing you could find nothing else to live on, Maskull\xe2\x80\x94would you eat\r\nother men?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI would not.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNeither will we eat plants and animals, which are our fellow creatures.\r\nSo nothing is left to us but water, and as one can really live on\r\nanything, water does very well.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull picked up one of the fruits and handled it curiously. As he did\r\nso another of his newly acquired sense organs came into action. He found\r\nthat the fleshy knobs beneath his ears were in some novel fashion\r\nacquainting him with the inward properties of the fruit. He could not\r\nonly see, feel, and smell it, but could detect its intrinsic nature.\r\nThis nature was hard, persistent and melancholy.\r\n\r\nJoiwind answered the questions he had not asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThose organs are called \xe2\x80\x98poigns.\xe2\x80\x99 Their use is to enable us to\r\nunderstand and sympathise with all living creatures.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat advantage do you derive from that, Joiwind?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe advantage of not being cruel and selfish, dear Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe threw the fruit away and flushed again.\r\n\r\nJoiwind looked into his swarthy, bearded face without embarrassment and\r\nslowly smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cHave I said too much? Have I been too familiar? Do you\r\nknow why you think so? It\xe2\x80\x99s because you are still impure. By and by you\r\nwill listen to all language without shame.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBefore he realised what she was about to do, she threw her tentacle\r\nround his neck, like another arm. He offered no resistance to its cool\r\npressure. The contact of her soft flesh with his own was so moist and\r\nsensitive that it resembled another kind of kiss. He saw who it was that\r\nembraced him\xe2\x80\x94a pale, beautiful girl. Yet, oddly enough, he experienced\r\nneither voluptuousness nor sexual pride. The love expressed by the\r\ncaress was rich, glowing, and personal, but there was not the least\r\ntrace of sex in it\xe2\x80\x94and so he received it.\r\n\r\nShe removed her tentacle, placed her two arms on his shoulders and\r\npenetrated with her eyes right into his very soul.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I wish to be pure,\xe2\x80\x9d he muttered. \xe2\x80\x9cWithout that what can I ever be\r\nbut a weak, squirming devil?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nJoiwind released him. \xe2\x80\x9cThis we call the \xe2\x80\x98magn,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d she said, indicating\r\nher tentacle. \xe2\x80\x9cBy means of it what we love already we love more, and\r\nwhat we don\xe2\x80\x99t love at all we begin to love.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA godlike organ!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is the one we guard most jealously,\xe2\x80\x9d said Joiwind.\r\n\r\nThe shade of the trees afforded a timely screen from the now almost\r\ninsufferable rays of Branchspell, which was climbing steadily upward to\r\nthe zenith. On descending the other side of the little hills, Maskull\r\nlooked anxiously for traces of Nightspore and Krag, but without result.\r\nAfter staring about him for a few minutes he shrugged his shoulders; but\r\nsuspicions had already begun to gather in his mind.\r\n\r\nA small, natural amphitheatre lay at their feet, completely circled by\r\nthe tree-clad heights. The centre was of red sand. In the very middle\r\nshot up a tall, stately tree, with a black trunk and branches, and\r\ntransparent, crystal leaves. At the foot of this tree was a natural,\r\ncircular well, containing dark green water.\r\n\r\nWhen they had reached the bottom, Joiwind took him straight over to the\r\nwell.\r\n\r\nMaskull gazed at it intently. \xe2\x80\x9cIs this the shrine you talked about?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes. It is called Shaping\xe2\x80\x99s Well. The man or woman who wishes to invoke\r\nShaping must take up some of the gnawl water, and drink it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPray for me,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cYour unspotted prayer will carry more\r\nweight.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you wish for?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor purity,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Maskull, in a troubled voice.\r\n\r\nJoiwind made a cup of her hand, and drank a little of the water. She\r\nheld it up to Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s mouth. \xe2\x80\x9cYou must drink too.\xe2\x80\x9d He obeyed. She then\r\nstood erect, closed her eyes, and, in a voice like the soft murmurings\r\nof spring, prayed aloud.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShaping, my father, I am hoping you can hear me. A strange man has come\r\nto us weighed down with heavy blood. He wishes to be pure. Let him know\r\nthe meaning of love, let him live for others. Don\xe2\x80\x99t spare him pain, dear\r\nShaping, but let him seek his own pain. Breathe into him a noble soul.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull listened with tears in his heart.\r\n\r\nAs Joiwind finished speaking, a blurred mist came over his eyes, and,\r\nhalf buried in the scarlet sand, appeared a large circle of dazzlingly\r\nwhite pillars. For some minutes they flickered to and fro between\r\ndistinctness and indistinctness, like an object being focused. Then they\r\nfaded out of sight again.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs that a sign from Shaping?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull, in a low, awed tone.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps it is. It is a time mirage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat can that be, Joiwind?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou see, dear Maskull, the temple does not yet exist but it will do so,\r\nbecause it must. What you and I are now doing in simplicity, wise men\r\nwill do hereafter in full knowledge.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is right for man to pray,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cGood and evil in the world\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t originate from nothing. God and Devil must exist. And we should\r\npray to the one, and fight the other.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, we must fight Krag.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat name did you say?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull in amazement.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKrag\xe2\x80\x94the author of evil and misery\xe2\x80\x94whom you call Devil.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe immediately concealed his thoughts. To prevent Joiwind from learning\r\nhis relationship to this being, he made his mind a blank.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy do you hide your mind from me?\xe2\x80\x9d she demanded, looking at him\r\nstrangely and changing colour.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn this bright, pure, radiant world, evil seems so remote, one can\r\nscarcely grasp its meaning.\xe2\x80\x9d But he lied.\r\n\r\nJoiwind continued gazing at him, straight out of her clean soul. \xe2\x80\x9cThe\r\nworld is good and pure, but many men are corrupt. Panawe, my husband,\r\nhas travelled, and he has told me things I would almost rather have not\r\nheard. One person he met believed the universe to be, from top to\r\nbottom, a conjurer\xe2\x80\x99s cave.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should like to meet your husband.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, we are going home now.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull was on the point of inquiring whether she had any children, but\r\nwas afraid of offending her, and checked himself.\r\n\r\nShe read the mental question. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat need is there? Is not the whole\r\nworld full of lovely children? Why should I want selfish possessions?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAn extraordinary creature flew past, uttering a plaintive cry of five\r\ndistinct notes. It was not a bird, but had a balloon-shaped body,\r\npaddled by five webbed feet. It disappeared among the trees.\r\n\r\nJoiwind pointed to it, as it went by. \xe2\x80\x9cI love that beast, grotesque as\r\nit is\xe2\x80\x94perhaps all the more for its grotesqueness.
