Between her and the fin\r\nthere was just room for Maskull. He grasped the two flanks with his\r\nouter hands; his third, new arm pressed against Oceaxe\xe2\x80\x99s back, and for\r\nadditional security he was compelled to encircle her waist with it.\r\n\r\nDirectly he did so, he realised that he had been tricked, and that this\r\nride had been planned for one purpose only\xe2\x80\x94to inflame his desires.\r\n\r\nThe third arm possessed a function of its own, of which hitherto he had\r\nbeen ignorant. It was a developed magn. But the stream of love which was\r\ncommunicated to it was no longer pure and noble\xe2\x80\x94it was boiling,\r\npassionate, and torturing. He gritted his teeth, and kept quiet, but\r\nOceaxe had not plotted the adventure to remain unconscious of his\r\nfeelings. She looked around, with a golden, triumphant smile. \xe2\x80\x9cThe ride\r\nwill last some time, so hold on well!\xe2\x80\x9d Her voice was soft like a flute,\r\nbut rather malicious.\r\n\r\nMaskull grinned, and said nothing. He dared not remove his arm.\r\n\r\nThe shrowk straddled on to its legs. It jerked itself forward, and rose\r\nslowly and uncouthly in the air. They began to paddle upward toward the\r\npainted cliffs. The motion was swaying, rocking, and sickening; the\r\ncontact of the brute\xe2\x80\x99s slimy skin was disgusting. All this, however, was\r\nmerely background to Maskull, as he sat there with closed eyes, holding\r\non to Oceaxe. In the front and centre of his consciousness was the\r\nknowledge that he was gripping a fair woman, and that her flesh was\r\nresponding to his touch like a lovely harp.\r\n\r\nThey climbed up and up. He opened his eyes, and ventured to look around\r\nhim. By this time they were already level with the top of the outer\r\nrampart of precipices. There now came in sight a wild archipelago of\r\nislands, with jagged outlines, emerging from a sea of air. The islands\r\nwere mountain summits; or, more accurately speaking, the country was a\r\nhigh tableland, fissured everywhere by narrow and apparently bottomless\r\ncracks. These cracks were in some cases like canals, in others like\r\nlakes, in others merely holes in the ground, closed in all round. The\r\nperpendicular sides of the islands\xe2\x80\x94that is, the upper, visible parts of\r\nthe innumerable cliff faces\xe2\x80\x94were of bare rock, gaudily coloured; but the\r\nlevel surfaces were a tangle of wild plant life. The taller trees alone\r\nwere distinguishable from the shrowk\xe2\x80\x99s back. They were of different\r\nshapes, and did not look ancient; they were slender and swaying but did\r\nnot appear very graceful; they looked tough, wiry, and savage.\r\n\r\nAs Maskull continued to explore the landscape, he forgot Oceaxe and his\r\npassion. Other strange feelings came to the front. The morning was gay\r\nand bright. The sun scorched down, quickly-changing clouds sailed across\r\nthe sky, the earth was vivid, wild, and lonely. Yet he experienced no\r\naesthetic sensations\xe2\x80\x94he felt nothing but an intense longing for action\r\nand possession. When he looked at anything, he immediately wanted to\r\ndeal with it. The atmosphere of the land seemed not free, but sticky;\r\nattraction and repulsion were its constituents. Apart from this wish to\r\nplay a personal part in what was going on around and beneath him, the\r\nscenery had no significance for him.\r\n\r\nSo preoccupied was he, that his arm partly released its clasp. Oceaxe\r\nturned around to gaze at him. Whether or not she was satisfied with what\r\nshe saw, she uttered a low laugh, like a peculiar chord.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCold again so quickly, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you want?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked absently, still looking over the side.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s extraordinary how drawn I feel to all this.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou wish to take a hand?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wish to get down.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, we have a good way to go yet.... So you really feel different?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDifferent from what? What are you talking about?\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, still\r\nlost in abstraction.\r\n\r\nOceaxe laughed again. \xe2\x80\x9cIt would be strange if we couldn\xe2\x80\x99t make a man of\r\nyou, for the material is excellent.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAfter that, she turned her back once more.\r\n\r\nThe air islands differed from water islands in another way. They were\r\nnot on a plane surface, but sloped upward, like a succession of broken\r\nterraces, as the journey progressed. The shrowk had hitherto been flying\r\nwell above the ground; but now, when a new line of towering cliffs\r\nconfronted them, Oceaxe did not urge the beast upward, but caused it to\r\nenter a narrow canyon, which intersected the mountains like a channel.\r\nThey were instantly plunged into deep shade. The canal was not above\r\nthirty feet wide; the walls stretched upward on both sides for many\r\nhundred feet. It was as cool as an ice chamber. When Maskull attempted\r\nto plumb the chasm with his eyes, he saw nothing but black obscurity.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is at the bottom?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDeath for you, if you go to look for it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe know that. I mean, is there any kind of life down there?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot that I have ever heard of,\xe2\x80\x9d said Oceaxe, \xe2\x80\x9cbut of course all things\r\nare possible.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think very likely there is life,\xe2\x80\x9d he returned thoughtfully.\r\n\r\nHer ironical laugh sounded out of the gloom. \xe2\x80\x9cShall we go down and see?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou find that amusing?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, not that. What I do find amusing is the big stranger with the\r\nbeard, who is so keenly interested in everything except himself.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull then laughed too. \xe2\x80\x9cI happen to be the only thing in Tormance\r\nwhich is not a novelty for me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, but I am a novelty for you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe channel went zigzagging its way through the belly of the mountain,\r\nand all the time they were gradually rising.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt least I have heard nothing like your voice before,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull,\r\nwho, since he had no longer anything to look at, was at last ready for\r\nconversation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s the matter with my voice?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s all that I can distinguish of you now; that\xe2\x80\x99s why I mentioned it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIsn\xe2\x80\x99t it clear\xe2\x80\x94don\xe2\x80\x99t I speak distinctly?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, it\xe2\x80\x99s clear enough, but\xe2\x80\x94it\xe2\x80\x99s inappropriate.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cInappropriate?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI won\xe2\x80\x99t explain further,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, \xe2\x80\x9cbut whether you are speaking\r\nor laughing, your voice is by far the loveliest and strangest instrument\r\nI have ever listened to. And yet I repeat, it is inappropriate.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou mean that my nature doesn\xe2\x80\x99t correspond?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe was just considering his reply, when their talk was abruptly broken\r\noff by a huge and terrifying, but not very loud sound rising up from the\r\ngulf directly underneath them. It was a low, grinding, roaring thunder.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe ground is rising under us!\xe2\x80\x9d cried Oceaxe.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShall we escape?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe made no answer, but urged the shrowk\xe2\x80\x99s flight upward, at such a\r\nsteep gradient that they retained their seats with difficulty. The floor\r\nof the canyon, upheaved by some mighty subterranean force, could be\r\nheard, and almost felt, coming up after them, like a gigantic landslip\r\nin the wrong direction. The cliffs cracked, and fragments began to fall.\r\nA hundred awful noises filled the air, growing louder and louder each\r\nsecond\xe2\x80\x94splitting, hissing, cracking, grinding, booming, exploding,\r\nroaring. When they had still fifty feet or so to go, to reach the top, a\r\nsort of dark, indefinite sea of broken rocks and soil appeared under\r\ntheir feet, ascending rapidly, with irresistible might, accompanied by\r\nthe most horrible noises. The canal was filled up for two hundred yards,\r\nbefore and behind them. Millions of tons of solid matter seemed to be\r\nraised. The shrowk in its ascent was caught by the uplifted debris.\r\nBeast and riders experienced in that moment all the horrors of an\r\nearthquake\xe2\x80\x94they were rolled violently over, and thrown among the rocks\r\nand dirt. All was thunder, instability, motion, confusion.\r\n\r\nBefore they had time to realise their position, they were in the\r\nsunlight. The upheaval still continued. In another minute or two the\r\nvalley floor had formed a new mountain, a hundred feet or more higher\r\nthan the old. Then its movement ceased suddenly. Every noise stopped, as\r\nif by magic; not a rock moved. Oceaxe and Maskull picked themselves up\r\nand examined themselves for cuts and bruises. The shrowk lay on its\r\nside, panting violently, and sweating with fright.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat was a nasty affair,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, flicking the dirt off his\r\nperson.\r\n\r\nOceaxe staunched a cut on her chin with a corner of her robe.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt might have been far worse.... I mean, it\xe2\x80\x99s bad enough to come up,\r\nbut it\xe2\x80\x99s death to go down, and that happens just as often.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhatever induces you to live in such a country?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know, Maskull. Habit, I suppose. I have often thought of moving\r\nout of it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA good deal must be forgiven you for having to spend your life in a\r\nplace like this, where one is obviously never safe from one minute to\r\nanother.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will learn by degrees,\xe2\x80\x9d she answered, smiling.\r\n\r\nShe looked hard at the monster, and it got heavily to its feet.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGet on again, Maskull!\xe2\x80\x9d she directed, climbing back to her perch. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\r\nhaven\xe2\x80\x99t too much time to waste.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe obeyed. They resumed their interrupted flight, this time over the\r\nmountains, and in full sunlight. Maskull settled down again to his\r\nthoughts. The peculiar atmosphere of the country continued to soak into\r\nhis brain. His will became so restless and uneasy that merely to sit\r\nthere in inactivity was a torture. He could scarcely endure not to be\r\ndoing something.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow secretive you are, Maskull!\xe2\x80\x9d said Oceaxe quietly, without turning\r\nher head.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat secrets\xe2\x80\x94what do you mean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, I know perfectly well what\xe2\x80\x99s passing inside you. Now I think it\r\nwouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be amiss to ask you\xe2\x80\x94is friendship still enough?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, don\xe2\x80\x99t ask me anything,\xe2\x80\x9d growled Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve far too many\r\nproblems in my head already. I only wish I could answer some of them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe stared stonily at the landscape. The beast was winging its way toward\r\na distant mountain, of singular shape. It was an enormous natural\r\nquadrilateral pyramid, rising in great terraces and terminating in a\r\nbroad, flat top, on which what looked like green snow still lingered.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat mountain is that?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDisscourn. The highest point in Ifdawn.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre we going there?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy should we go there? But if you were going on farther, it might be\r\nworth your while to pay a visit to the top. It commands the whole land\r\nas far as the Sinking Sea and Swaylone\xe2\x80\x99s Island\xe2\x80\x94and beyond. You can also\r\nsee Alppain from it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a sight I mean to see before I have finished.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d She turned around and put her hand on his wrist.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStay with me, and one day we\xe2\x80\x99ll go to Disscourn together.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe grunted unintelligibly.\r\n\r\nThere were no signs of human existence in the country under their feet.\r\nWhile Maskull was still grimly regarding it, a large tract of forest not\r\nfar ahead, bearing many trees and rocks, suddenly subsided with an awful\r\nroar and crashed down into an invisible gulf. What was solid land one\r\nminute became a clean-cut chasm the next. He jumped violently up with\r\nthe shock. \xe2\x80\x9cThis is frightful.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nOceaxe remained unmoved.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, life here must be absolutely impossible,\xe2\x80\x9d he went on, when he had\r\nsomewhat recovered himself. \xe2\x80\x9cA man would need nerves of steel.... Is\r\nthere no means at all of foreseeing a catastrophe like this?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, I suppose we wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be alive if there weren\xe2\x80\x99t,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Oceaxe,\r\nwith composure. \xe2\x80\x9cWe are more or less clever at it\xe2\x80\x94but that doesn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nprevent our often getting caught.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou had better teach me the signs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ll have many things to go over together. And among them, I expect,\r\nwill be whether we are to stay in the land at all.... But first let us\r\nget home.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow far is it now?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is right in front of you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Oceaxe, pointing with her\r\nforefinger. \xe2\x80\x9cYou can see it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe followed the direction of the finger and, after a few questions, made\r\nout the spot she was indicating. It was a broad peninsula, about two\r\nmiles distant. Three of its sides rose sheer out of a lake of air, the\r\nbottom of which was invisible; its fourth was a bottleneck, joining it\r\nto the mainland. It was overgrown with bright vegetation, distinct in\r\nthe brilliant atmosphere. A single tall tree, shooting up in the middle\r\nof the peninsula, dwarfed everything else; it was wide and shady with\r\nsea-green leaves.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wonder if Crimtyphon is there,\xe2\x80\x9d remarked Oceaxe. \xe2\x80\x9cCan I see two\r\nfigures, or am I mistaken?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI also see something,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\nIn twenty minutes they were directly above the peninsula, at a height of\r\nabout fifty feet. The shrowk slackened speed, and came to earth on the\r\nmainland, exactly at the gateway of the isthmus. They both\r\ndescended\xe2\x80\x94Maskull with aching thighs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat shall we do with the monster?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Oceaxe. Without waiting for a\r\nsuggestion, she patted its hideous face with her hand. \xe2\x80\x9cFly away home! I\r\nmay want you some other time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIt gave a stupid grunt, elevated itself on its legs again, and, after\r\nhalf running, half flying for a few yards, rose awkwardly into the air,\r\nand paddled away in the same direction from which they had come. They\r\nwatched it out of sight, and then Oceaxe started to cross the neck of\r\nland, followed by Maskull.\r\n\r\nBranchspell\xe2\x80\x99s white rays beat down on them with pitiless force. The sky\r\nhad by degrees become cloudless, and the wind had dropped entirely. The\r\nground was a rich riot of vividly coloured ferns, shrubs, and grasses.\r\nThrough these could be seen here and there the golden chalky soil\xe2\x80\x94and\r\noccasionally a glittering, white metallic boulder. Everything looked\r\nextraordinary and barbaric. Maskull was at last walking in the weird\r\nIfdawn Marest which had created such strange feelings in him when seen\r\nfrom a distance.... And now he felt no wonder or curiosity at all, but\r\nonly desired to meet human beings\xe2\x80\x94so intense had grown his will. He\r\nlonged to test his powers on his fellow creatures, and nothing else\r\nseemed of the least importance to him.\r\n\r\nOn the peninsula all was coolness and delicate shade. It resembled a\r\nlarge copse, about two acres in extent. In the heart of the tangle of\r\nsmall trees and undergrowth was a partially cleared space\xe2\x80\x94perhaps the\r\nroots of the giant tree growing in the centre had killed off the smaller\r\nfry all around it. By the side of the tree sparkled a little, bubbling\r\nfountain, whose water was iron-red. The precipices on all sides,\r\noverhung with thorns, flowers, and creepers, invested the enclosure with\r\nan air of wild and charming seclusion\xe2\x80\x94a mythological mountain god might\r\nhave dwelt here.\r\n\r\nMaskull\xe2\x80\x99s restless eye left everything, to fall on the two men who\r\nformed the centre of the picture.\r\n\r\nOne was reclining, in the ancient Grecian fashion of banqueters on a\r\ntall couch of mosses, sprinkled with flowers; he rested on one arm, and\r\nwas eating a kind of plum, with calm enjoyment. A pile of these plums\r\nlay on the couch beside him. The over-spreading branches of the tree\r\ncompletely sheltered him from the sun. His small, boyish form was clad\r\nin a rough skin, leaving his limbs naked. Maskull could not tell from\r\nhis face whether he were a young boy or a grown man. The features were\r\nsmooth, soft, and childish, their expression was seraphically tranquil;\r\nbut his violet upper eye was sinister and adult. His skin was of the\r\ncolour of yellow ivory. His long, curling hair matched his sorb\xe2\x80\x94it was\r\nviolet. The second man was standing erect before the other, a few feet\r\naway from him. He was short and muscular, his face was broad, bearded,\r\nand rather commonplace, but there was something terrible about his\r\nappearance. The features were distorted by a deep-seated look of pain,\r\ndespair, and horror.\r\n\r\nOceaxe, without pausing, strolled lightly and lazily up to the outermost\r\nshadows of the tree, some distance from the couch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have met with an uplift,\xe2\x80\x9d she remarked carelessly, looking toward\r\nthe youth.\r\n\r\nHe eyed her, but said nothing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow is your plant man getting on?\xe2\x80\x9d Her tone was artificial but\r\nextremely beautiful. While waiting for an answer, she sat down on the\r\nground, her legs gracefully thrust under her body, and pulled down the\r\nskirt of her robe. Maskull remained standing just behind her, with\r\ncrossed arms.\r\n\r\nThere was silence for a minute.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy don\xe2\x80\x99t you answer your mistress, Sature?\xe2\x80\x9d said the boy on the couch,\r\nin a calm, treble voice.\r\n\r\nThe man addressed did not alter his expression, but replied in a\r\nstrangled tone, \xe2\x80\x9cI am getting on very well, Oceaxe. There are already\r\nbuds on my feet. Tomorrow I hope to take root.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull felt a rising storm inside him. He was perfectly aware that\r\nalthough these words were uttered by Sature, they were being dictated by\r\nthe boy.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat he says is quite true,\xe2\x80\x9d remarked the latter. \xe2\x80\x9cTomorrow roots will\r\nreach the ground, and in a few days they ought to be well established.\r\nThen I shall set to work to convert his arms into branches, and his\r\nfingers into leaves. It will take longer to transform his head into a\r\ncrown, but still I hope\xe2\x80\x94in fact I can almost promise that within a month\r\nyou and I, Oceaxe, will be plucking and enjoying fruit from this new and\r\nremarkable tree.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI love these natural experiments,\xe2\x80\x9d he concluded, putting out his hand\r\nfor another plum. \xe2\x80\x9cThey thrill me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis must be a joke,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, taking a step forward.\r\n\r\nThe youth looked at him serenely. He made no reply, but Maskull felt as\r\nif he were being thrust backward by an iron hand on his throat.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe morning\xe2\x80\x99s work is now concluded, Sature. Come here again after\r\nBlodsombre. After tonight you will remain here permanently, I expect, so\r\nyou had better set to work to clear a patch of ground for your roots.\r\nNever forget\xe2\x80\x94however fresh and charming these plants appear to you now,\r\nin the future they will be your deadliest rivals and enemies. Now you\r\nmay go.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe man limped painfully away, across the isthmus, out of sight. Oceaxe\r\nyawned.\r\n\r\nMaskull pushed his way forward, as if against a wall. \xe2\x80\x9cAre you joking,\r\nor are you a devil?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am Crimtyphon. I never joke. For that epithet of yours, I will devise\r\na new punishment for you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe duel of wills commenced without ceremony. Oceaxe got up, stretched\r\nher beautiful limbs, smiled, and prepared herself to witness the\r\nstruggle between her old lover and her new. Crimtyphon smiled too; he\r\nreached out his hand for more fruit, but did not eat it. Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s self-\r\ncontrol broke down and he dashed at the boy, choking with red fury\xe2\x80\x94his\r\nbeard wagged and his face was crimson. When he realised with whom he had\r\nto deal, Crimtyphon left off smiling, slipped off the couch, and threw a\r\nterrible and malignant glare into his sorb. Maskull staggered. He\r\ngathered together all the brute force of his will, and by sheer weight\r\ncontinued his advance. The boy shrieked and ran behind the couch, trying\r\nto get away.... His opposition suddenly collapsed. Maskull stumbled\r\nforward, recovered himself, and then vaulted clear over the high pile of\r\nmosses, to get at his antagonist. He fell on top of him with all his\r\nbulk. Grasping his throat, he pulled his little head completely around,\r\nso that the neck was broken. Crimtyphon immediately died.\r\n\r\nThe corpse lay underneath the tree with its face upturned. Maskull\r\nviewed it attentively, and as he did so an expression of awe and wonder\r\ncame into his own countenance. In the moment of death Crimtyphon\xe2\x80\x99s face\r\nhad undergone a startling and even shocking alteration. Its personal\r\ncharacter had wholly vanished, giving place to a vulgar, grinning mask\r\nwhich expressed nothing.\r\n\r\nHe did not have to search his mind long, to remember where he had seen\r\nthe brother of that expression. It was identical with that on the face\r\nof the apparition at the siance, after Krag had dealt with it.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nChapter 10. TYDOMIN\r\n\r\nOceaxe sat down carelessly on the couch of mosses, and began eating the\r\nplums.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou see, you had to kill him, Maskull,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, in a rather quizzical\r\nvoice.\r\n\r\nHe came away from the corpse and regarded her\xe2\x80\x94still red, and still\r\nbreathing hard. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s no joking matter. You especially ought to keep\r\nquiet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause he was your husband.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou think I ought to show grief\xe2\x80\x94when I feel none?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t pretend, woman!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nOceaxe smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cFrom your manner one would think you were accusing me of\r\nsome crime.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull literally snorted at her words. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat, you live with filth\xe2\x80\x94you\r\nlive in the arms of a morbid monstrosity and then\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, now I grasp it,\xe2\x80\x9d she said, in a tone of perfect detachment.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m glad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, Maskull,\xe2\x80\x9d she proceeded, after a pause, \xe2\x80\x9cand who gave you the\r\nright to rule my conduct? Am I not mistress of my own person?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe looked at her with disgust, but said nothing. There was another long\r\ninterval of silence.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI never loved him,\xe2\x80\x9d said Oceaxe at last, looking at the ground.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat makes it all the worse.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat does all this mean\xe2\x80\x94what do you want?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing from you\xe2\x80\x94absolutely nothing\xe2\x80\x94thank heaven!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe gave a hard laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cYou come here with your foreign preconceptions\r\nand expect us all to bow down to them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat preconceptions?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cJust because Crimtyphon\xe2\x80\x99s sports are strange to you, you murder him\xe2\x80\x94and\r\nyou would like to murder me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSports! That diabolical cruelty.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, you\xe2\x80\x99re sentimental!\xe2\x80\x9d said Oceaxe contemptuously. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy do you need\r\nto make such a fuss over that man? Life is life, all the world over, and\r\none form is as good as another. He was only to be made a tree, like a\r\nmillion other trees. If they can endure the life, why can\xe2\x80\x99t he?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd this is Ifdawn morality!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nOceaxe began to grow angry. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s you who have peculiar ideas. You rave\r\nabout the beauty of flowers and trees\xe2\x80\x94you think them divine. But when\r\nit\xe2\x80\x99s a question of taking on this divine, fresh, pure, enchanting\r\nloveliness yourself, in your own person, it immediately becomes a cruel\r\nand wicked degradation. Here we have a strange riddle, in my opinion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOceaxe, you\xe2\x80\x99re a beautiful, heartless wild beast\xe2\x80\x94nothing more. For this you may\r\nthank my \xe2\x80\x98foreign preconceptions.\xe2\x80\x99... Farewell!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe turned to go. Oceaxe\xe2\x80\x99s eyes slanted at him through their long lashes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere are you off to, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a matter of no importance, for wherever I go it must be a change\r\nfor the better. We can quickly put that\r\nbody out of sight, and, as you seem to detest me so much, the place is\r\nbig enough\xe2\x80\x94we needn\xe2\x80\x99t talk, or even see each other.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t wish to breathe the same air.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSingular man!\xe2\x80\x9d She was sitting erect and motionless, like a beautiful\r\nstatue. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd what of your wonderful interview with Surtur, and all the\r\nundone things which you set out to do?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou aren\xe2\x80\x99t the one I shall speak to about that. Ought\r\nthey not to?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI once heard it called \xe2\x80\x98Crystalman\xe2\x80\x99s face.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy not? It was from Alppain, but Alppain itself was behind the hills. While\r\nhe was observing it, a peculiar wave of self-denial, of a disquieting\r\nnature, passed through him. Don\xe2\x80\x99t you know\r\nthat?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nDuring the pause that followed, a snapping of twigs was heard, and both\r\nlooked around, startled. They saw a woman stepping slowly across the\r\nneck that separated them from the mainland.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTydomin,\xe2\x80\x9d muttered Oceaxe, in a vexed, frightened voice. She\r\nimmediately moved away from Maskull and stood up.\r\n\r\nThe newcomer was of middle height, very slight and graceful. She was no\r\nlonger quite young. Her face wore the composure of a woman who knows her\r\nway about the world. It was intensely pale, and under its quiescence\r\nthere just was a glimpse of something strange and dangerous. It was\r\ncuriously alluring, though not exactly beautiful. Her hair was\r\nclustering and boyish, reaching only to the neck. It was of a strange\r\nindigo colour. She was quaintly attired in a tunic and breeches, pieced\r\ntogether from the square, blue-green plates of some reptile. Her small,\r\nivory-white breasts were exposed. Her sorb was black and sad\xe2\x80\x94rather\r\ncontemplative.\r\n\r\nWithout once glancing up at Oceaxe and Maskull, she quietly glided\r\nstraight toward Crimtyphon\xe2\x80\x99s corpse. When she arrived within a few feet\r\nof it, she stopped and looked down, with arms folded.\r\n\r\nOceaxe drew Maskull a little away, and whispered, \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s Crimtyphon\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nother wife, who lives under Disscourn. She\xe2\x80\x99s a most dangerous woman. Be\r\ncareful what you say. If she asks you to do anything, refuse it\r\noutright.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe poor soul looks harmless enough.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, she does\xe2\x80\x94but the poor soul is quite capable of swallowing up Krag\r\nhimself.... Now, play the man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe murmur of their voices seemed to attract Tydomin\xe2\x80\x99s notice, for she\r\nnow slowly turned her eyes toward them.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho killed him?\xe2\x80\x9d she demanded.\r\n\r\nHer voice was so soft, low, and refined, that Maskull hardly was able to\r\ncatch the words. The sounds, however, lingered in his ears, and\r\ncuriously enough seemed to grow stronger, instead of fainter.\r\n\r\nOceaxe whispered, \xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t say a word, leave it all to me.\xe2\x80\x9d Then she swung\r\nher body around to face Tydomin squarely, and said aloud, \xe2\x80\x9cI killed\r\nhim.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin\xe2\x80\x99s words by this time were ringing in Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s head like an\r\nactual physical sound. Their path lay through\r\nsunshine and shadow. Branchspell was blazing in a cloudless sky, the\r\nheat was insufferable\xe2\x80\x94streams of sweat coursed down his face, and the\r\ncorpse seemed to grow heavier and heavier. They had to pass\r\nfrom peak to peak, as from island to island. In some cases they were\r\nable to stride or jump across, but in others they had to make use of\r\nrude bridges of fallen timber. It appeared to be a frequented path.\r\nUnderneath were the black, impenetrable abysses\xe2\x80\x94on the surface were the\r\nglaring sunshine, the gay, painted rocks, the chaotic tangle of strange\r\nplants. One monstrous insect, as large\r\nas a horse, stood right in the centre of their path without budging. It\r\nwas armour-plated, had jaws like scimitars, and underneath its body was\r\na forest of legs. Tydomin gave one malignant look at it, and sent it\r\ncrashing into the gulf.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat have I to offer, except my life?\xe2\x80\x9d Maskull suddenly broke out. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd\r\nwhat good is that? It\xe2\x80\x99s a penalty which we pay.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI know that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe point is whether you can go on enjoying life, after what has\r\nhappened.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe waited for Maskull to come even with her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps you imagine I\xe2\x80\x99m not man enough\xe2\x80\x94you imagine that because I\r\nallowed poor Oceaxe to die for me\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe did die for you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin, in a quiet, emphatic voice.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat would be a second blunder of yours,\xe2\x80\x9d returned Maskull, just as\r\nfirmly. \xe2\x80\x9cI was not in love with Oceaxe, and I\xe2\x80\x99m not in love with life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour life is not required.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen I don\xe2\x80\x99t understand what you want, or what you are speaking about.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not for me to ask a sacrifice from you, Maskull. Beyond its farther edge the\r\nAlppain glow burned blue just over the horizon.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow we shall have to make a detour,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin, halting.\r\n\r\nMaskull caught hold of her with his third hand. \xe2\x80\x9cListen to me, while I\r\ntry to describe what I\xe2\x80\x99m feeling. Then, where the land was, we now have\r\nthis empty, awful gulf\xe2\x80\x94that\xe2\x80\x99s to say, nothing\xe2\x80\x94and it seems to me as if\r\nour life will come to the same condition, where there was something\r\nthere will be nothing. At the same time, it is grand and\r\njoyful. The joy consists in this\xe2\x80\x94that it is in our power to give freely\r\nwhat will later on be taken from us by force.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin watched him attentively. \xe2\x80\x9cThen your feeling is that your life is\r\nworthless, and you make a present of it to the first one who asks?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, it goes beyond that. A little later on, in a narrow copse crowning a miniature,\r\ninsulated peak, they fell in with a man. He was resting himself against\r\na tree, and looked tired, overheated, and despondent. He was young. His\r\nbeardless expression bore an expression of unusual sincerity, and in\r\nother respects he seemed a hardy, hardworking youth, of an intellectual\r\ntype. He felt no immediate difference in his soul, but...\r\n\r\nTydomin shed a sad smile on him, like winter sunshine. He half expected\r\nher to speak, but she said nothing. The mountaintops became loftier\r\nand more widely separated from one another. The gaps were filled with\r\nrolling, white clouds, which bathed the shores of the peaks like a\r\nmysterious sea. To pass from island to island was hard work, the\r\nintervening spaces were so wide\xe2\x80\x94Tydomin, however, knew the way. The\r\nintense light, the violet-blue sky, the patches of vivid landscape,\r\nemerging from the white vapour-ocean, made a profound impression on\r\nMaskull\xe2\x80\x99s mind. The glow of Alppain was hidden by the huge mass of\r\nDisscourn, which loomed up straight in front of them.\r\n\r\nThe green snow on the top of the gigantic pyramid had by now completely\r\nmelted away. Tydomin pointed to a small black hole near the base,\r\nwhich might be a cave. \xe2\x80\x9cThat is where I live.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou live here alone?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s an odd choice for a woman\xe2\x80\x94and you are not unbeautiful, either.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA woman\xe2\x80\x99s life is over at twenty-five,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, sighing. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd I am\r\nfar older than that. Then all this wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t have happened.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n*****\r\n\r\nA quarter of an hour later they stood within the mouth of the cave. It\r\nwas ten feet high, and its interior was impenetrably black.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPut down the body in the entrance, out of the sun,\xe2\x80\x9d directed Tydomin.\r\nHe did so.\r\n\r\nShe cast a keenly scrutinising glance at him. \xe2\x80\x9cDoes your resolution\r\nstill hold, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t it hold? At that very moment a sickening crash,\r\nlike heavy thunder just over their heads, set Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s weakened heart\r\nthumping violently. An avalanche of boulders, stones, and dust, swept\r\npast the cave entrance from above. If their going in had been delayed by\r\na single minute, they would have been killed.\r\n\r\nTydomin did not even look up. She took his hand in hers, and started\r\nwalking with him into the darkness. The temperature became as cold as\r\nice. At the first bend the light from the outer world disappeared,\r\nleaving them in absolute blackness. Maskull kept stumbling over the\r\nuneven ground, but she kept tight hold of him, and hurried him along.\r\n\r\nThe tunnel seemed of interminable length. Presently, however, the\r\natmosphere changed\xe2\x80\x94or such was his impression. He was somehow led to\r\nimagine that they had come to a larger chamber. His groping hand\r\nencountered stone and, by feeling it all over, he discovered that it was\r\na sort of stone slab, or couch, raised a foot or eighteen inches from\r\nthe ground. I make no other supplication.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nChapter 11. ON DISSCOURN\r\n\r\nBY THE TIME that they regained the mouth of the cavern, Blodsombre was\r\nat its height. Behind them the\r\nbright, stupendous crags of Disscourn loomed up for a thousand feet or\r\nmore. Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s eyes were red, and his face looked stupid; he was still\r\nholding the woman by the arm. She made no attempt to speak, or to get\r\naway. She seemed perfectly gentle and composed.\r\n\r\nAfter gazing at the country for a long time in silence, he turned toward\r\nher. \xe2\x80\x9cWhereabouts is the fiery lake you spoke of?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt lies on the other side of the mountain. Rather than be alone, I\xe2\x80\x99ll come with you\xe2\x80\x94but you know that if I\r\nset foot in Sant they will kill me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt least set me on the way. I wish to get there before night. Is it\r\npossible?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you are willing to take risks with nature. And why should you not\r\ntake risks today? Your luck holds. But someday or other it won\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nhold\xe2\x80\x94your luck.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet us start,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cThe luck I\xe2\x80\x99ve had so far is nothing to\r\nbrag about.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBlodsombre was over when they set off; it was early afternoon, but the\r\nheat seemed more stifling than ever. They made no more pretence at\r\nconversation; both were buried in their own painful thoughts. The land\r\nfell away from Disscourn in all other directions, but toward Sant there\r\nwas a gentle, persistent rise. Its dark, distant plateau continued to\r\ndominate the landscape, and after walking for an hour they seemed none\r\nthe nearer to it. The air was stale and stagnant.\r\n\r\nBy and by, an upright object, apparently the work of man, attracted\r\nMaskull\xe2\x80\x99s notice. It was a slender tree stem, with the bark still on,\r\nimbedded in the stony ground. From the upper end three branches sprang\r\nout, pointing aloft at a sharp angle. They were stripped to twigs and\r\nleaves and, getting closer, he saw that they had been artificially\r\nfastened on, at equal distances from each other.\r\n\r\nAs he stared at the object, a strange, sudden flush of confident vanity\r\nand self-sufficiency seemed to pass through him, but it was so momentary\r\nthat he could be sure of nothing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat may that be, Tydomin?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is Hator\xe2\x80\x99s Trifork.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd what is its purpose?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a guide to Sant.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut who or what is Hator?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHator was the founder of Sant\xe2\x80\x94many thousands of years ago. He laid down\r\nthe principles they all live by, and that trifork is his symbol. When I\r\nwas a little child my father told me the legends, but I\xe2\x80\x99ve forgotten\r\nmost of them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull regarded it attentively.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDoes it affect you in any way?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd why should it do that?\xe2\x80\x9d she said, dropping her lip scornfully. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nam only a woman, and these are masculine mysteries.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA sort of gladness came over me,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, \xe2\x80\x9cbut perhaps I am\r\nmistaken.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey passed on. The scenery gradually changed in character. The solid\r\nparts of the land grew more continuous, the fissures became narrower and\r\nmore infrequent. There were now no more subsidences or upheavals. The\r\npeculiar nature of the Ifdawn Marest appeared to be giving place to a\r\ndifferent order of things.\r\n\r\nLater on, they encountered a flock of pale blue jellies floating in the\r\nair. They were miniature animals. Tydomin caught one in her hand and\r\nbegan to eat it, just as one eats a luscious pear plucked from a tree.\r\nMaskull, who had fasted since early morning, was not slow in following\r\nher example. A sort of electric vigour at once entered his limbs and\r\nbody, his muscles regained their elasticity, his heart began to beat\r\nwith hard, slow, strong throbs.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFood and body seem to agree well in this world,\xe2\x80\x9d he remarked smiling.\r\n\r\nShe glanced toward him. \xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps the explanation is not in the food, but\r\nin your body.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI brought my body with me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou brought your soul with you, but that\xe2\x80\x99s altering fast, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIn a copse they came across a short, wide tree, without leaves, but\r\npossessing a multitude of thin, flexible branches, like the tentacles of\r\na cuttlefish. Some of these branches were moving rapidly. A furry\r\nanimal, somewhat resembling a wildcat, leaped about among them in the\r\nmost extraordinary way. But the next minute Maskull was shocked to\r\nrealise that the beast was not leaping at all, but was being thrown from\r\nbranch to branch by the volition of the tree, exactly as an imprisoned\r\nmouse is thrown by a cat from paw to paw.\r\n\r\nHe watched the spectacle a while with morbid interest.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a gruesome reversal of r\xc3\xb4les, Tydomin.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne can see you\xe2\x80\x99re disgusted,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, stifling a yawn. \xe2\x80\x9cBut that\r\nis because you are a slave to words. If you called that plant an animal,\r\nyou would find its occupation perfectly natural and pleasing. And why\r\nshould you not call it an animal?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am quite aware that, as long as I remain in the Ifdawn Marest, I\r\nshall go on listening to this sort of language.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey trudged along for an hour or more without talking. The day became\r\novercast. A thin mist began to shroud the landscape, and the sun changed\r\ninto an immense ruddy disk which could be stared at without flinching. A\r\nchill, damp wind blew against them. Presently it grew still darker, the\r\nsun disappeared and, glancing first at his companion and then at\r\nhimself, Maskull noticed that their skin and clothing were coated by a\r\nkind of green hoarfrost.\r\n\r\nThe land was now completely solid. About half a mile, in front of them,\r\nagainst a background of dark fog, a moving forest of tall waterspouts\r\ngyrated slowly and gracefully hither and thither. They were green and\r\nself-luminous, and looked terrifying. Tydomin explained that they were\r\nnot waterspouts at all, but mobile columns of lightning.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen they are dangerous?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo we think,\xe2\x80\x9d she answered, watching them closely.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSomeone is wandering there who appears to have a different opinion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAmong the spouts, and entirely encompassed by them, a man was walking\r\nwith a slow, calm, composed gait, his back turned toward Maskull and\r\nTydomin. There was something unusual in his appearance\xe2\x80\x94his form looked\r\nextraordinarily distinct, solid, and real.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf there\xe2\x80\x99s danger, he ought to be warned,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe who is always anxious to teach will learn nothing,\xe2\x80\x9d returned the\r\nwoman coolly. She restrained Maskull by a pressure of the arm, and\r\ncontinued to watch.\r\n\r\nThe base of one of the columns touched the man. He remained unharmed,\r\nbut turned sharply around, as if for the first time made aware of the\r\nproximity of these deadly waltzers. Then he raised himself to his full\r\nheight, and stretched both arms aloft above his head, like a diver. He\r\nseemed to be addressing the columns.\r\n\r\nWhile they looked on, the electric spouts discharged themselves, with a\r\nseries of loud explosions. The stranger stood alone, uninjured. He\r\ndropped his arms. The next moment he caught sight of the two, and stood\r\nstill, waiting for them to come up. The pictorial clarity of his person\r\ngrew more and more noticeable as they approached; his body seemed to be\r\ncomposed of some substance heavier and denser than solid matter.\r\n\r\nTydomin looked perplexed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe must be a Sant man. I have seen no one quite like him before. This\r\nis a day of days for me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe must be an individual of great importance,\xe2\x80\x9d murmured Maskull.\r\n\r\nThey now came up to him. He was tall, strong, and bearded, and was\r\nclothed in a shirt and breeches of skin. Since turning his back to the\r\nwind, the green deposit on his face and limbs had changed to streaming\r\nmoisture, through which his natural colour was visible; it was that of\r\npale iron. There was no third arm. His face was harsh and frowning, and\r\na projecting chin pushed the beard forward. On his forehead there were\r\ntwo flat membranes, like rudimentary eyes, but no sorb. These membranes\r\nwere expressionless, but in some strange way seemed to add vigour to the\r\nstern eyes underneath. When his glance rested on Maskull, the latter\r\nfelt as though his brain were being thoroughly travelled through. The\r\nman was middle-aged.\r\n\r\nHis physical distinctness transcended nature. By contrast with him,\r\nevery object in the neighbourhood looked vague and blurred. Tydomin\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nperson suddenly appeared faint, sketch-like, without significance, and\r\nMaskull realised that it was no better with himself. A queer, quickening\r\nfire began running through his veins.\r\n\r\nHe turned to the woman. \xe2\x80\x9cIf this man is going to Sant, I shall bear him\r\ncompany. We can now part. No doubt you will think it high time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet Tydomin come too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe words were delivered in a rough, foreign tongue, but were as\r\nintelligible to Maskull as if spoken in English.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou who know my name, also know my sex,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin quietly. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is\r\ndeath for me to enter Sant.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is the old law. I am the bearer of the new law.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs it so\xe2\x80\x94and will it be accepted?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe old skin is cracking, the new skin has been silently forming\r\nunderneath, the moment of sloughing has arrived.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe storm gathered. The green snow drove against them, as they stood\r\ntalking, and it grew intensely cold. None noticed it.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is your name?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull, with a beating heart.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy name, Maskull, is Spadevil. You, a voyager across the dark ocean of\r\nspace, shall be my first witness and follower. You, Tydomin, a daughter\r\nof the despised sex, shall be my second.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe new law? But what is it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cUntil eye sees, of what use it is for ear to hear?.... Come, both of\r\nyou, to me!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin went to him unhesitatingly. Spadevil pressed his hand on her\r\nsorb and kept it there for a few minutes, while he closed his own eyes.\r\nWhen he removed it, Maskull observed that the sorb was transformed into\r\ntwin membranes like Spadevil\xe2\x80\x99s own.\r\n\r\nTydomin looked dazed. She glanced quietly about for a little while,\r\napparently testing her new faculty. Then the tears started to her eyes\r\nand, snatching up Spadevil\xe2\x80\x99s hand, she bent over and kissed it hurriedly\r\nmany times.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy past has been bad,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cNumbers have received harm from me,\r\nand none good. I have killed\xe2\x80\x94and worse. But now I can throw all that\r\naway, and laugh. Nothing can now injure me. Oh, Maskull, you and I have\r\nbeen fools together!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t you repent your crimes?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLeave the past alone,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil, \xe2\x80\x9cit cannot be reshaped. The\r\nfuture alone is ours. It starts fresh and clean from this very minute.\r\nWhy do you hesitate, Maskull? Are you afraid?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the name of those organs, and what is their function?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey are probes, and they are the gates opening into a new world.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull lingered no longer, but permitted Spadevil to cover his sorb.\r\n\r\nWhile the iron hand was still pressing his forehead, the new law quietly\r\nflowed into his consciousness, like a smooth-running stream of clean\r\nwater which had hitherto been dammed by his obstructive will. The law\r\nwas duty.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nChapter 12. SPADEVIL\r\n\r\nMaskull found that his new organs had no independent function of their\r\nown, but only intensified and altered his other senses. When he used his\r\neyes, ears, or nostrils, the same objects presented themselves to him,\r\nbut his judgment concerning them was different. Previously all external\r\nthings had existed for him; now he existed for them. According to\r\nwhether they served his purpose or were in harmony with his nature, or\r\notherwise, they had been pleasant or painful. Now these words \xe2\x80\x9cpleasure\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nand \xe2\x80\x9cpain\xe2\x80\x9d simply had no meaning.\r\n\r\nThe other two watched him, while he was making himself acquainted with\r\nhis new mental outlook. He smiled at them.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou were quite right, Tydomin,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, in a bold, cheerful voice. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\r\nhave been fools. So near the light all the time, and we never guessed\r\nit. Always buried in the past or future\xe2\x80\x94systematically ignoring the\r\npresent\xe2\x80\x94and now it turns out that apart from the present we have no life\r\nat all.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThank Spadevil for it,\xe2\x80\x9d she answered, more loudly than usual.\r\n\r\nMaskull looked at the man\xe2\x80\x99s dark, concrete form. \xe2\x80\x9cSpadevil, now I mean\r\nto follow you to the end. I can do nothing less.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe severe face showed no sign of gratification\xe2\x80\x94not a muscle relaxed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWatch that you don\xe2\x80\x99t lose your gift,\xe2\x80\x9d he said gruffly.\r\n\r\nTydomin spoke. \xe2\x80\x9cYou promised that I should enter Sant with you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAttach yourself to the truth, not to me. For I may die before you, but\r\nthe truth will accompany you to your death. However, now let us journey\r\ntogether, all three of us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe words had not left his mouth before he put his face against the\r\nfine, driving snow, and pressed onward toward his destination. He walked\r\nwith a long stride; Tydomin was obliged to half run in order to keep up\r\nwith him. The three travelled abreast; Spadevil in the middle. The fog\r\nwas so dense that it was impossible to see a hundred yards ahead. The\r\nground was covered by the green snow. The wind blew in gusts from the\r\nSant highlands and was piercingly cold.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSpadevil, are you a man, or more than a man?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe that is not more than a man is nothing.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere have you now come from?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom brooding, Maskull. Out of no other mother can truth be born. I\r\nhave brooded, and rejected; and I have brooded again. Now, after many\r\nmonths\xe2\x80\x99 absence from Sant, the truth at last shines forth for me in its\r\nsimple splendour, like an upturned diamond.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI see its shining,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cBut how much does it owe to ancient\r\nHator?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cKnowledge has its seasons. The blossom was to Hator, the fruit is to\r\nme. Hator also was a brooder\xe2\x80\x94but now his followers do not brood. In Sant\r\nall is icy selfishness, a living death. They hate pleasure, and this\r\nhatred is the greatest pleasure to them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut in what way have they fallen off from Hator\xe2\x80\x99s doctrines?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor him, in his sullen purity of nature, all the world was a snare, a\r\nlimed twig. Knowing that pleasure was everywhere, a fierce, mocking\r\nenemy, crouching and waiting at every corner of the road of life, in\r\norder to kill with its sweet sting the naked grandeur of the soul, he\r\nshielded himself behind pain. This also his followers do, but they do\r\nnot do it for the sake of the soul, but for the sake of vanity and\r\npride.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the Trifork?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe stem, Maskull, is hatred of pleasure. The first fork is\r\ndisentanglement from the sweetness of the world. The second fork is\r\npower over those who still writhe in the nets of illusion. The third\r\nfork is the healthy glow of one who steps into ice-cold water.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFrom what land did Hator come?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is not said. He lived in Ifdawn for a while. There are many legends\r\ntold of him while there.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have a long way to go,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin. \xe2\x80\x9cRelate some of these legends,\r\nSpadevil.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe snow had ceased, the day brightened, Branchspell reappeared like a\r\nphantom sun, but bitter blasts of wind still swept over the plain.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn those days,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil, \xe2\x80\x9cthere existed in Ifdawn a mountain\r\nisland separated by wide spaces from the land around it. A handsome\r\ngirl, who knew sorcery, caused a bridge to be constructed across which\r\nmen and women might pass to it. Having by a false tale drawn Hator on to\r\nthis rock, she pushed at the bridge with her foot until it tumbled into\r\nthe depths below. \xe2\x80\x98You and I, Hator, are now together, and there is no\r\nmeans of separating. I wish to see how long the famous frost man can\r\nwithstand the breath, smiles and perfume of a girl.\xe2\x80\x99 Hator said no word,\r\neither then or all that day. He stood till sunset like a tree trunk, and\r\nthought of other things. Then the girl grew passionate, and shook her\r\ncurls. She rose from where she was sitting she looked at him, and\r\ntouched his arm; but he did not see her. She looked at him, so that all\r\nthe soul was in her eyes; and then she fell down dead. Hator awoke from\r\nhis thoughts, and saw her lying, still warm, at his feet, a corpse. He\r\npassed to the mainland; but how, it is not related.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin shuddered. \xe2\x80\x9cYou too have met your wicked woman, Spadevil; but\r\nyour method is a nobler one.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t pity other women,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil, \xe2\x80\x9cbut love the right. Hator also\r\nonce conversed with Shaping.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWith the Maker of the World?\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull thoughtfully.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWith the Maker of Pleasure. It is told how Shaping defended his world,\r\nand tried to force Hator to acknowledge loveliness and joy. But Hator,\r\nanswering all his marvellous speeches in a few concise, iron words,\r\nshowed how this joy and beauty was but another name for the bestiality\r\nof souls wallowing in luxury and sloth. Shaping smiled, and said, \xe2\x80\x98How\r\ncomes it that your wisdom is greater than that of the Master of wisdom?\xe2\x80\x99\r\nHator said, \xe2\x80\x98My wisdom does not come from you, nor from your world, but\r\nfrom that other world, which you, Shaping, have vainly tried to\r\nimitate.\xe2\x80\x99 Shaping replied, \xe2\x80\x98What, then, do you do in my world?\xe2\x80\x99 Hator\r\nsaid, \xe2\x80\x98I am here falsely, and therefore I am subject to your false\r\npleasures. But I wrap myself in pain\xe2\x80\x94not because it is good, but because\r\nI wish to keep myself as far from you as possible. For pain is not\r\nyours, neither does it belong to the other world, but it is the shadow\r\ncast by your false pleasures.\xe2\x80\x99 Shaping then said, \xe2\x80\x98What is this faraway\r\nother world of which you say \xe2\x80\x9cThis is so\xe2\x80\x94this is not so?\xe2\x80\x9d How happens it\r\nthat you alone of all my creatures have knowledge of it?\xe2\x80\x99 But Hator spat\r\nat his feet, and said, \xe2\x80\x98You lie, Shaping. All have knowledge of it. You,\r\nwith your pretty toys, alone obscure it from our view.\xe2\x80\x99 Shaping asked,\r\n\xe2\x80\x98What, then, am I?\xe2\x80\x99 Hator answered, \xe2\x80\x98You are the dreamer of impossible\r\ndreams.\xe2\x80\x99 And then the story goes that Shaping departed, ill pleased with\r\nwhat had been said.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat other world did Hator refer to?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOne where grandeur reigns, Maskull, just as pleasure reigns here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhether grandeur or pleasure, it makes no difference,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe individual spirit that lives and wishes to live is mean and\r\ncorrupt-natured.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGuard you your pride!\xe2\x80\x9d returned Spadevil. \xe2\x80\x9cDo not make law for the\r\nuniverse and for all time, but for yourself and for this small, false\r\nlife of yours.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn what shape did death come to that hard, unconquerable man?\xe2\x80\x9d asked\r\nTydomin.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe lived to be old, but went upright and free-limbed to his last hour.\r\nWhen he saw that death could not be staved off longer he determined to\r\ndestroy himself. He gathered his friends around him; not from vanity,\r\nbut that they might see to what lengths the human soul can go in its\r\nperpetual warfare with the voluptuous body. Standing erect, without\r\nsupport, he died by withholding his breath.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nA silence followed, which lasted for perhaps an hour. Their minds\r\nrefused to acknowledge the icy winds, but the current of their thoughts\r\nbecame frozen.\r\n\r\nWhen Branchspell, however, shone out again, though with subdued power,\r\nMaskull\xe2\x80\x99s curiosity rose once more. \xe2\x80\x9cYour fellow countrymen, then,\r\nSpadevil, are sick with self-love?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe men of other countries,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil, \xe2\x80\x9care the slaves of pleasure\r\nand desire, knowing it. But the men of my country are the slaves of\r\npleasure and desire, not knowing it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd yet that proud pleasure, which rejoices in self-torture, has\r\nsomething noble in it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe who studies himself at all is ignoble. Only by despising soul as\r\nwell as body can a man enter into true life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn what grounds do they reject women?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cInasmuch as a woman has ideal love, and cannot live for herself. Love\r\nfor another is pleasure for the loved one, and therefore injurious to\r\nhim.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA forest of false ideas is waiting for your axe,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cBut\r\nwill they allow it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSpadevil knows, Maskull,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin, \xe2\x80\x9cthat be it today or be it\r\ntomorrow, love can\xe2\x80\x99t be kept out of a land, even by the disciples of\r\nHator.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBeware of love\xe2\x80\x94beware of emotion!\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Spadevil. \xe2\x80\x9cLove is but\r\npleasure once removed. Think not of pleasing others, but of serving\r\nthem.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cForgive me, Spadevil, if I am still feminine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRight has no sex. So long, Tydomin, as you remember that you are a\r\nwoman, so long you will not enter into divine apathy of soul.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut where there are no women, there are no children,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow came there to be all these generations of Hator men?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLife breeds passion, passion breeds suffering, suffering breeds the\r\nyearning for relief from suffering. Men throng to Sant from all parts,\r\nin order to have the scars of their souls healed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn place of hatred of pleasure, which all can understand, what simple\r\nformula do you offer?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIron obedience to duty,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Spadevil.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd if they ask \xe2\x80\x98How far is this consistent with hatred of pleasure?\xe2\x80\x99\r\nwhat will your pronouncement be?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI do not answer them, but I answer you, Maskull, who ask the question.\r\nHatred is passion, and all passion springs from the dark fires of self.\r\nDo not hate pleasure at all, but pass it by on one side, calm and\r\nundisturbed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the criterion of pleasure? How can we always recognise it, in\r\norder to avoid it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRigidly follow duty, and such questions will not arise.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nLater in the afternoon, Tydomin timidly placed her fingers on Spadevil\xe2\x80\x99s\r\narm.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFearful doubts are in my mind,\xe2\x80\x9d she said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis expedition to Sant may\r\nturn out badly. I have seen a vision of you, Spadevil, and myself lying\r\ndead and covered in blood, but Maskull was not there.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe may drop the torch, but it will not be extinguished, and others will\r\nraise it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShow me a sign that you are not as other men\xe2\x80\x94so that I may know that\r\nour blood will not be wasted.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil regarded her sternly. \xe2\x80\x9cI am not a magician. I don\xe2\x80\x99t persuade\r\nthe senses, but the soul. Does your duty call you to Sant, Tydomin? Then\r\ngo there. Does it not call you to Sant? Then go no farther. Is not this\r\nsimple? What signs are necessary?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDid I not see you dispel those spouts of lightning? No common man could\r\nhave done that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho knows what any man can do? This man can do one thing, that man can\r\ndo another. But what all men can do is their duty; and to open their\r\neyes to this, I must go to Sant, and if necessary lay down my life. Will\r\nyou not still accompany me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin, \xe2\x80\x9cI will follow you to the end. It is all the more\r\nessential, because I keep on displeasing you with my remarks, and that\r\nmeans I have not yet learned my lesson properly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo not be humble, for humility is only self-judgment, and while we are\r\nthinking of self, we must be neglecting some action we could be planning\r\nor shaping in our mind.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin continued to be uneasy and preoccupied.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy was Maskull not in the picture?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou dwell on this foreboding because you imagine it is tragical. There\r\nis nothing tragical in death, Tydomin, nor in life. There is only right\r\nand wrong. What arises from right or wrong action does not matter. We\r\nare not gods, constructing a world, but simple men and women, doing our\r\nimmediate duty. We may die in Sant\xe2\x80\x94so you have seen it; but the truth\r\nwill go on living.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSpadevil, why do you choose Sant to start your work in?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThese men with fixed ideas seem to me the least likely of any to follow\r\na new light.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere a bad tree thrives, a good tree will flourish. But where no tree\r\nat all can be found, nothing will grow.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI understand you,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cHere perhaps we are going to\r\nmartyrdom, but elsewhere we should resemble men preaching to cattle.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShortly before sunset they arrived at the extremity of the upland plain,\r\nabove which towered the black cliffs of the Sant Levels. A dizzy,\r\nartificially constructed staircase, of more than a thousand steps of\r\nvarying depth, twisting and forking in order to conform to the angles of\r\nthe precipices, led to the world overhead. In the place where they stood\r\nthey were sheltered from the cutting winds. Branchspell, radiantly\r\nshining at last, but on the point of sinking, filled the cloudy sky with\r\nviolent, lurid colors, some of the combinations of which were new to\r\nMaskull. The circle of the horizon was so gigantic, that had he been\r\nsuddenly carried back to Earth, he would by comparison have fancied\r\nhimself to be moving beneath the dome of some little, closed-in\r\ncathedral. He realised that he was on a foreign planet. But he was not\r\nstirred or uplifted by the knowledge; he was conscious only of moral\r\nideas. Looking backward, he saw the plain, which for several miles past\r\nhad been without vegetation, stretching back away to Disscourn. So\r\nregular had been the ascent, and so great was the distance, that the\r\nhuge pyramid looked nothing more than a slight swelling on the face of\r\nthe earth.\r\n\r\nSpadevil stopped, and gazed over the landscape in silence. In the\r\nevening sunlight his form looked more dense, dark, and real than ever\r\nbefore. His features were set hard in grimness.\r\n\r\nHe turned around to his companions. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the greatest wonder, in all\r\nthis wonderful scene?\xe2\x80\x9d he demanded.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAcquaint us,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAll that you see is born from pleasure, and moves on, from pleasure to\r\npleasure. Nowhere is right to be found. It is Shaping\xe2\x80\x99s world.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere is another wonder,\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin, and she pointed her finger\r\ntoward the sky overhead.\r\n\r\nA small cloud, so low down that it was perhaps not more than five\r\nhundred feet above them, was sailing along in front of the dark wall of\r\ncliff. It was in the exact shape of an open human hand, with downward-\r\npointing fingers. It was stained crimson by the sun; and one or two tiny\r\ncloudlets beneath the fingers looked like falling drops of blood.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho can doubt now that our death is close at hand?\xe2\x80\x9d said Tydomin. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nhave been close to death twice today. The first time I was ready, but\r\nnow I am more ready, for I shall die side by side with the man who has\r\ngiven me my first happiness.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo not think of death, but of right persistence,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Spadevil. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\nam not here to tremble before Shaping\xe2\x80\x99s portents; but to snatch men from\r\nhim.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe at once proceeded to lead the way up the staircase. Tydomin gazed\r\nupward after him for a moment, with an odd, worshiping light in her\r\neyes. Then she followed him, the second of the party. Maskull climbed\r\nlast. He was travel stained, unkempt, and very tired; but his soul was\r\nat peace. As they steadily ascended the almost perpendicular stairs, the\r\nsun got higher in the sky. Its light dyed their bodies a ruddy gold.\r\n\r\nThey gained the top. There they found rolling in front of them, as far\r\nas the eye could see, a barren desert of white sand, broken here and\r\nthere by large, jagged masses of black rock. Tracts of the sand were\r\nreddened by the sinking sun. The vast expanse of sky was filled by evil-\r\nshaped clouds and wild colors. The freezing wind, flurrying across the\r\ndesert, drove the fine particles of sand painfully against their faces.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere now do you take us?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe who guards the old wisdom of Sant must give up that wisdom to me,\r\nthat I may change it. What he says, others will say. I go to find\r\nMaulger.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd where will you seek him, in this bare country?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil struck off toward the north unhesitatingly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is not so far,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt is his custom to be in that part where\r\nSant overhangs the Wombflash Forest. Perhaps he will be there, but I\r\ncannot say.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull glanced toward Tydomin. Her sunken cheeks, and the dark circles\r\nbeneath her eyes told of her extreme weariness.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe woman is tired, Spadevil,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\r\n\r\nShe smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s but another step into the land of death. I can manage\r\nit. Give me your arm, Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe put his arm around her waist, and supported her along that way.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe sun is now sinking,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cWill we get there before dark?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFear nothing, Maskull and Tydomin; this pain is eating up the evil in\r\nyour nature. The road you are walking cannot remain unwalked. We shall\r\narrive before dark.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe sun then disappeared behind the far-distant ridges that formed the\r\nwestern boundary of the Ifdawn Marest. The sky blazed up into more vivid\r\ncolors. The wind grew colder.\r\n\r\nThey passed some pools of colourless gnawl water, round the banks of\r\nwhich were planted fruit trees. Maskull ate some of the fruit. It was\r\nhard, bitter, and astringent; he could not get rid of the taste, but he\r\nfelt braced and invigorated by the downward-flowing juices. No other\r\ntrees or shrubs were to be seen anywhere. No animals appeared, no birds\r\nor insects. It was a desolate land.\r\n\r\nA mile or two passed, when they again approached the edge of the\r\nplateau. Far down, beneath their feet, the great Wombflash Forest began.\r\nBut daylight had vanished there; Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s eyes rested only on a vague\r\ndarkness. He faintly heard what sounded like the distant sighing of\r\ninnumerable treetops.\r\n\r\nIn the rapidly darkening twilight, they came abruptly on a man. He was\r\nstanding in a pool, on one leg. A pile of boulders had hidden him from\r\ntheir view. The water came as far up as his calf. A trifork, similar to\r\nthe one Maskull had seen on Disscourn, but smaller, had been stuck in\r\nthe mud close by his hand.\r\n\r\nThey stopped by the side of the pond, and waited. Immediately he became\r\naware of their presence, the man set down his other leg, and waded out\r\nof the water toward them, picking up his trifork in doing so.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is not Maulger, but Catice,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMaulger is dead,\xe2\x80\x9d said Catice, speaking the same tongue as Spadevil,\r\nbut with an even harsher accent, so that the tympanum of Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s ear\r\nwas affected painfully.\r\n\r\nThe latter saw before him a bowed, powerful individual, advanced in\r\nyears. He wore nothing but a scanty loincloth. His trunk was long and\r\nheavy, but his legs were rather short. His face was beardless, lemon-\r\ncoloured, and anxious-looking. It was disfigured by a number of\r\nlongitudinal ruts, a quarter of an inch deep, the cavities of which\r\nseemed clogged with ancient dirt. The hair of his head was black and\r\nsparse. Instead of the twin membranous organs of Spadevil, he possessed\r\nbut one; and this was in the centre of his brow.\r\n\r\nSpadevil\xe2\x80\x99s dark, solid person stood out from the rest like a reality\r\namong dreams.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHas the trifork passed to you?\xe2\x80\x9d he demanded.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes. Why have you brought this woman to Sant?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have brought another thing to Sant. I have brought the new faith.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCatice stood motionless, and looked troubled. \xe2\x80\x9cState it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShall I speak with many words, or few words?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you wish to say what is not, many words will not suffice. If you\r\nwish to say what is, a few words will be enough.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil frowned.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo hate pleasure brings pride with it. Pride is a pleasure. To kill\r\npleasure, we must attach ourselves to duty. While the mind is planning\r\nright action, it has no time to think of pleasure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs that the whole?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Catice.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe truth is simple, even for the simplest man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you destroy Hator, and all his generations, with a single word?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI destroy nature, and set up law.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nA long silence followed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy probe is double,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil. \xe2\x80\x9cSuffer me to double yours, and you\r\nwill see as I see.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome you here, you big man!\xe2\x80\x9d said Catice to Maskull. Maskull advanced a\r\nstep closer.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you follow Spadevil in his new faith?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs far as death,\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Maskull.\r\n\r\nCatice picked up a flint. \xe2\x80\x9cWith this stone I strike out one of your two\r\nprobes. When you have but one, you will see with me, and you will\r\nrecollect with Spadevil. Choose you then the superior faith, and I shall\r\nobey your choice.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEndure this little pain, Maskull, for the sake of future men,\xe2\x80\x9d said\r\nSpadevil.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe pain is nothing,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Maskull, \xe2\x80\x9cbut I fear the result.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPermit me, although I am only a woman, to take his place, Catice,\xe2\x80\x9d said\r\nTydomin, stretching out her hand.\r\n\r\nHe struck at it violently with the flint, and gashed it from wrist to\r\nthumb; the pale carmine blood spouted up. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat brings this kiss-lover\r\nto Sant?\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cHow does she presume to make the rules of life for\r\nthe sons of Hator?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe bit her lip, and stepped back. \xe2\x80\x9cWell then, Maskull, accept! I\r\ncertainly should not have played false to Spadevil; but you hardly can.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf he bids me, I must do it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cBut who knows what will\r\ncome of it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil spoke. \xe2\x80\x9cOf all the descendants of Hator, Catice is the most\r\nwholehearted and sincere. He will trample my truth underfoot, thinking\r\nme a demon sent by Shaping, to destroy the work of this land. But a seed\r\nwill escape, and my blood and yours, Tydomin, will wash it. Then men\r\nwill know that my destroying evil is their greatest good. But none here\r\nwill live to see that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull now went quite close to Catice, and offered his head. Catice\r\nraised his hand, and after holding the flint poised for a moment,\r\nbrought it down with adroitness and force upon the left-hand probe.\r\nMaskull cried out with the pain. The blood streamed down, and the\r\nfunction of the organ was destroyed.\r\n\r\nThere was a pause, while he walked to and fro, trying to staunch the\r\nblood.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat now do you feel, Maskull? What do you see?\xe2\x80\x9d inquired Tydomin\r\nanxiously.\r\n\r\nHe stopped, and stared hard at her. \xe2\x80\x9cI now see straight,\xe2\x80\x9d he said\r\nslowly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat does that mean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe continued to wipe the blood from his forehead. He looked troubled.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHenceforward, as long as I live, I shall fight with my nature, and\r\nrefuse to feel pleasure. And I advise you to do the same.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil gazed at him sternly. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you renounce my teaching?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull, however, returned the gaze without dismay. Spadevil\xe2\x80\x99s image-\r\nlike clearness of form had departed for him; his frowning face he knew\r\nto be the deceptive portico of a weak and confused intellect.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is false.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs it false to sacrifice oneself for another?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded Tydomin.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t argue as yet,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cAt this moment the world with its\r\nsweetness seems to me a sort of charnel house. I feel a loathing for\r\neverything in it, including myself. I know no more.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs there no duty?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Spadevil, in a harsh tone.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt appears to me but a cloak under which we share the pleasure of other\r\npeople.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin pulled at Spadevil\xe2\x80\x99s arm. \xe2\x80\x9cMaskull has betrayed you, as he has\r\nso many others. Let us go.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe stood fast. \xe2\x80\x9cYou have changed quickly, Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull, without answering him, turned to Catice. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy do men go on\r\nliving in this soft, shameful world, when they can kill themselves?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPain is the native air of Surtur\xe2\x80\x99s children. To what other air do you\r\nwish to escape?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSurtur\xe2\x80\x99s children? Is not Surtur Shaping?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is the greatest of lies. It is Shaping\xe2\x80\x99s masterpiece.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnswer, Maskull!\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you repudiate right action?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLeave me alone. Go back! I am not thinking of you, and your ideas. I\r\nwish you no harm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe darkness came on fast. There was another prolonged silence.\r\n\r\nCatice threw away the flint, and picked up his staff. \xe2\x80\x9cThe woman must\r\nreturn home,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe was persuaded here, and did not come freely. You, Spadevil, must\r\ndie\xe2\x80\x94backslider as you are!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin said quietly, \xe2\x80\x9cHe has no power to enforce this. Are you going to\r\nallow the truth to fall to the ground, Spadevil?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt will not perish by my death, but by my efforts to escape from death.\r\nCatice, I accept your judgment.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTydomin smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cFor my part, I am too tired to walk farther today, so I\r\nshall die with him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCatice said to Maskull, \xe2\x80\x9cProve your sincerity. Kill this man and his\r\nmistress, according to the laws of Hator.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t do that. I have travelled in friendship with them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou denied duty; and now you must do your duty,\xe2\x80\x9d said Spadevil, calmly\r\nstroking his beard. \xe2\x80\x9cWhatever law you accept, you must obey, without\r\nturning to right or left. Your law commands that we must be stoned; and\r\nit will soon be dark.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you not even this amount of manhood?\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Tydomin.\r\n\r\nMaskull moved heavily. \xe2\x80\x9cBe my witness, Catice, that the thing was forced\r\non me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHator is looking on, and approving,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Catice.\r\n\r\nMaskull then went apart to the pile of boulders scattered by the side of\r\nthe pool. He glanced about him, and selected two large fragments of\r\nrock, the heaviest that he thought he could carry. With these in his\r\narms, he staggered back.\r\n\r\nHe dropped them on the ground, and stood, recovering his breath. When he\r\ncould speak again, he said, \xe2\x80\x9cI have a bad heart for the business. Is\r\nthere no alternative? Sleep here tonight, Spadevil, and in the morning\r\ngo back to where you have come from. No one shall harm you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSpadevil\xe2\x80\x99s ironic smile was lost in the gloom.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShall I brood again, Maskull, for still another year, and after that\r\ncome back to Sant with other truths?
