Muspel\r\ncan\xe2\x80\x99t be willed, for the simple reason that Muspel does not concern the\r\nwill. To will is a property of this world.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen what is your journey for?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s one thing to walk to a destination, and to linger over the walk,\r\nand quite another to run there at top speed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps I\xe2\x80\x99m not so easily deceived as you think,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang with\r\nanother smile.\r\n\r\nThe light persisted in the cave. The path narrowed and became a steep\r\nascent. Then the angle became one of forty-five degrees, and they had to\r\nclimb. The tunnel grew so confined that Maskull was reminded of the\r\nconfined dreams of his childhood.\r\n\r\nNot long afterward, daylight appeared. They hastened to complete the\r\nlast stage. Maskull rushed out first into the world of colours and, all\r\ndirty and bleeding from numerous scratches, stood blinking on a\r\nhillside, bathed in the brilliant late-afternoon sunshine. Corpang\r\nfollowed closely at his heels. He was obliged to shield his eyes with\r\nhis hands for a few minutes, so unaccustomed was he to Branchspell\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nblinding rays.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe drum beats have stopped!\xe2\x80\x9d he exclaimed suddenly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou can\xe2\x80\x99t expect music all the time,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Maskull dryly. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\r\nmustn\xe2\x80\x99t be luxurious.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut now we have no guide. We\xe2\x80\x99re no better off than before.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, Tormance is a big place. But I have an infallible rule, Corpang.\r\nAs I come from the south, I always go due north.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat will take us to Lichstorm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull gazed at the fantastically piled rocks all around them. \xe2\x80\x9cI saw\r\nthese rocks from Matterplay. The mountains look as far off now as they\r\ndid then, and there\xe2\x80\x99s not much of the day left. How far is Lichstorm\r\nfrom here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang looked away to the distant range. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know, but unless a\r\nmiracle happens we shan\xe2\x80\x99t get there tonight.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have a feeling,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, \xe2\x80\x9cthat we shall not only get there\r\ntonight, but that tonight will be the most important in my life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd he sat down passively to rest.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nChapter 18. HAUNTE\r\n\r\nWhile Maskull sat, Corpang walked restlessly to and fro, swinging his\r\narms. He had lost his staff. His face was inflamed with suppressed\r\nimpatience, which accentuated its natural coarseness. At last he stopped\r\nshort in front of Maskull and looked down at him. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you intend to\r\ndo?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull glanced up and idly waved his hand toward the distant mountains.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSince we can\xe2\x80\x99t walk, we must wait.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor what?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t know... How\xe2\x80\x99s this, though? Those peaks have changed colour,\r\nfrom red to green.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, the lich wind is travelling this way.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe lich wind?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the atmosphere of Lichstorm. It always clings to the mountains,\r\nbut when the wind blows from the north it comes as far as Threal.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a sort of fog, then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA peculiar sort, for they say it excites the sexual passions.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo we are to have lovemaking,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, laughing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps you won\xe2\x80\x99t find it so joyous,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Corpang a little grimly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut tell me\xe2\x80\x94these peaks, how do they preserve their balance?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang gazed at the distant, overhanging summits, which were fast\r\nfading into obscurity.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPassion keeps them from falling.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull laughed again; he was feeling a strange disturbance of spirit.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat, the love of rock for rock?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is comical, but true.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ll take a closer peep at them presently. Beyond the mountains is\r\nBarey, is it not?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd then the Ocean. But what is the name of that Ocean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is told only to those who die beside it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs the secret so precious, Corpang?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBranchspell was nearing the horizon in the west; there were more than\r\ntwo hours of daylight remaining. The air all around them became murky.\r\nIt was a thin mist, neither damp nor cold. The Lichstorm Range now\r\nappeared only as a blur on the sky. The air was electric and tingling,\r\nand was exciting in its effect. Maskull felt a sort of emotional\r\ninflammation, as though a very slight external cause would serve to\r\noverturn his self-control. Corpang stood silent with a mouth like iron.\r\n\r\nMaskull kept looking toward a high pile of rocks in the vicinity.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat seems to me a good watchtower. Perhaps we shall see something from\r\nthe top.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWithout waiting for his companion\xe2\x80\x99s opinion, he began to scramble up the\r\ntor, and in a few minutes was standing on the summit. Corpang joined\r\nhim.\r\n\r\nFrom their viewpoint they saw the whole countryside sloping down to the\r\nsea, which appeared as a mere flash of far-off, glittering water.\r\nLeaving all that, however, Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s eyes immediately fastened\r\nthemselves on a small, boat-shaped object, about two miles away, which\r\nwas travelling rapidly toward them, suspended only a few feet in the\r\nair.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you make of that?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked in a tone of astonishment.\r\n\r\nCorpang shook his head and said nothing.\r\n\r\nWithin two minutes the flying object, whatever it was, had diminished\r\nthe distance between them by one half. It resembled a boat more and\r\nmore, but its flight was erratic, rather than smooth; its nose was\r\ncontinually jerking upward and downward, and from side to side. Maskull\r\nnow made out a man sitting in the stern, and what looked like a large\r\ndead animal lying amidships. As the aerial craft drew nearer, he\r\nobserved a thick, blue haze underneath it, and a similar haze behind,\r\nbut the front, facing them, was clear.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere must be what we are waiting for, Corpang. But what on earth\r\ncarries it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe stroked his beard contemplatively, and then, fearing that they had\r\nnot been seen, stepped onto the highest rock, bellowed loudly, and made\r\nwild motions with his arm. The flying-boat, which was only a few hundred\r\nyards distant, slightly altered its course, now heading toward them in a\r\nway that left no doubt that the steersman had detected their presence.\r\n\r\nThe boat slackened speed until it was travelling no faster than a\r\nwalking man, but the irregularity of its movements continued. It was\r\nshaped rather queerly. About twenty feet long, its straight sides\r\ntapered off from a flat bow, four feet broad, to a sharp-angled stern.\r\nThe flat bottom was not above ten feet from the ground. It was undecked,\r\nand carried only one living occupant; the other object they had\r\ndistinguished was really the carcass of an animal, of about the size of\r\na large sheep. The blue haze trailing behind the boat appeared to\r\nemanate from the glittering point of a short upright pole fastened in\r\nthe stern. When the craft was within a few feet of them, and they were\r\nlooking down at it in wonder from above, the man removed this pole and\r\ncovered the brightly shining tip with a cap. The forward motion then\r\nceased altogether, and the boat began to drift hither and thither, but\r\nstill it remained suspended in the air, while the haze underneath\r\npersisted. Finally the broad side came gently up against the pile of\r\nrocks on which they were standing. The steersman jumped ashore and\r\nimmediately clambered up to meet them.\r\n\r\nMaskull offered him a hand, but he refused it disdainfully. He was a\r\nyoung man, of middle height. He wore a close-fitting fur garment. His\r\nlimbs were quite ordinary, but his trunk was disproportionately long,\r\nand he had the biggest and deepest chest that Maskull had ever seen in a\r\nman. His hairless face was sharp, pointed, and ugly, with protruding\r\nteeth, and a spiteful, grinning expression. His eyes and brows sloped\r\nupward. On his forehead was an organ which looked as though it had been\r\nmutilated\xe2\x80\x94it was a mere disagreeable stump of flesh. His hair was short\r\nand thin. Maskull could not name the colour of his skin, but it seemed\r\nto stand in the same relation to jale as green to red.\r\n\r\nOnce up, the stranger stood for a minute or two, scrutinising the two\r\ncompanions through half-closed lids, all the time smiling insolently.\r\nMaskull was all eagerness to exchange words, but did not care to be the\r\nfirst to speak. Corpang stood moodily, a little in the background.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat men are you?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded the aerial navigator at last. His voice was\r\nextremely loud, and possessed a most unpleasant timbre. It sounded to\r\nMaskull like a large volume of air trying to force its way through a\r\nnarrow orifice.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am Maskull; my friend is Corpang. He comes from Threal, but where I\r\ncome from, don\xe2\x80\x99t ask.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am Haunte, from Sarclash.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere may that be?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHalf an hour ago I could have shown it to you, but now it has got too\r\nmurky. It is a mountain in Lichstorm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you returning there now?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd how long will it take to get there in that boat?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTwo\xe2\x80\x94three hours.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWill it accommodate us too?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat, are you for Lichstorm as well? What can you want there?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo see the sights,\xe2\x80\x9d responded Maskull with twinkling eyes. \xe2\x80\x9cBut first\r\nof all, to dine. I can\xe2\x80\x99t remember having eaten all day. You seem to have\r\nbeen hunting to some purpose, so we won\xe2\x80\x99t lack for food.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte eyed him quizzically. \xe2\x80\x9cYou certainly don\xe2\x80\x99t lack impudence.\r\nHowever, I\xe2\x80\x99m a man of that sort myself, and it is the sort I prefer.\r\nYour friend, now, would probably rather starve than ask a meal of a\r\nstranger. He looks to me just like a bewildered toad dragged up out of a\r\ndark hole.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull took Corpang\xe2\x80\x99s arm, and constrained him to silence.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere have you been hunting, Haunte?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMatterplay. I had the worst luck\xe2\x80\x94I speared one wold horse, and there it\r\nlies.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is Lichstorm like?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere are men there, and there are women there, but there are no men-\r\nwomen, as with you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you call men-women?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPersons of mixed sex, like yourself. In Lichstorm the sexes are pure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have always regarded myself as a man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery likely you have; but the test is, do you hate and fear women?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, do you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte grinned and showed his teeth. \xe2\x80\x9cThings are different in\r\nLichstorm.... So you want to see the sights?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI confess I am curious to see your women, for example, after what you\r\nsay.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen I\xe2\x80\x99ll introduce you to Sullenbode.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe paused a moment after making this remark, and then suddenly uttered a\r\ngreat, bass laugh, so that his chest shook.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet us share the joke,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, you\xe2\x80\x99ll understand it later.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf you play pranks with me, I won\xe2\x80\x99t stand on ceremony with you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte laughed again. \xe2\x80\x9cI won\xe2\x80\x99t be the one to play pranks. Sullenbode\r\nwill be deeply obliged to me. If I don\xe2\x80\x99t visit her myself as often as\r\nshe would like, I\xe2\x80\x99m always glad to serve her in other ways.... Well, you\r\nshall have your boat ride.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull rubbed his nose doubtfully. \xe2\x80\x9cIf the sexes hate one another in\r\nyour land, is it because passion is weaker, or stronger?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn other parts of the world there is soft passion, but in Lichstorm\r\nthere is hard passion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what do you call hard passion?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere men are called to women by pain, and not pleasure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI intend to understand, before I\xe2\x80\x99ve finished.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d answered Haunte, with a taunting look, \xe2\x80\x9cit would be a pity to let\r\nthe chance slip, since you\xe2\x80\x99re going to Lichstorm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIt was now Corpang\xe2\x80\x99s turn to take Maskull by the arm. \xe2\x80\x9cThis journey will\r\nend badly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy so?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour goal was Muspel a short while ago; now it is women.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet me alone,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cGive luck a slack rein. What brought this\r\nboat here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is this talk about Muspel?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded Haunte.\r\n\r\nCorpang caught his shoulder roughly, and stared straight into his eyes.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you know?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot much, but something, perhaps. Ask me at supper. Now it is high time\r\nto start. Navigating the mountains by night isn\xe2\x80\x99t child\xe2\x80\x99s play, let me\r\ntell you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall not forget,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang.\r\n\r\nMaskull gazed down at the boat. \xe2\x80\x9cAre we to get in?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGently, my friend. It\xe2\x80\x99s only canework and skin.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFirst of all, you might enlighten me as to how you have contrived to\r\ndispense with the laws of gravitation.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte smiled sarcastically. \xe2\x80\x9cA secret in your ear, Maskull. All laws\r\nare female. A true male is an outlaw\xe2\x80\x94outside the law.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t understand.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe great body of the earth is continually giving out female particles,\r\nand the male parts of rocks and living bodies are equally continually\r\ntrying to reach them. That\xe2\x80\x99s gravitation.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen how do you manage with your boat?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy two male stones do the work. The one underneath the boat prevents it\r\nfrom falling to the ground; the one in the stern shuts it off from solid\r\nobjects in the rear. The only part of the boat attracted by any part of\r\nthe earth is the bow, for that\xe2\x80\x99s the only part the light of the male\r\nstones does not fall on. So in that direction the boat travels.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd what are these wondrous male stones?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey really are male stones. There is nothing female in them; they are\r\nshowering out male sparks all the time. These sparks devour all the\r\nfemale particles rising from the earth. No female particles are left\r\nover to attract the male parts of the boat, and so they are not in the\r\nleast attracted in that direction.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull ruminated for a minute.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWith your hunting, and boatbuilding, and science, you seem a very\r\nhandy, skilful fellow, Haunte.... But the sun\xe2\x80\x99s sinking, and we\xe2\x80\x99d better\r\nstart.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGet down first, then, and shift that carcass farther forward. Then you\r\nand your gloomy friend can sit amidships.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull immediately climbed down, and dropped himself into the boat; but\r\nthen he received a surprise. The moment he stood on the frail bottom,\r\nstill clinging to the rock, not only did his weight entirely disappear,\r\nas though he were floating in some heavy medium, like salt water, but\r\nthe rock he held onto drew him, as by a mild current of electricity, and\r\nhe was able to withdraw his hands only with difficulty.\r\n\r\nAfter the first moment\xe2\x80\x99s shock, he quietly accepted the new order of\r\nthings, and set about shifting the carcass. Since there was no weight in\r\nthe boat this was effected without any great labour. Corpang then\r\ndescended. The astonishing physical change had no power to disturb his\r\nsettled composure, which was founded on moral ideas. Haunte came last;\r\ngrasping the staff which held the upper male stone, he proceeded to\r\nerect it, after removing the cap. Maskull then obtained his first near\r\nview of the mysterious light, which, by counteracting the forces of\r\nNature, acted indirectly not only as elevator but as motive force. In\r\nthe last ruddy gleams of the great sun, its rays were obscured, and it\r\nlooked little more impressive than an extremely brilliant, scintillating\r\nblue-white jewel, but its power could be gauged by the visible, coloured\r\nmist that it threw out for many yards around.\r\n\r\nThe steering was effected by means of a shutter attached by a cord to\r\nthe top of the staff, which could be so manipulated that any segment of\r\nthe male stone\xe2\x80\x99s rays, or all the rays, or none at all, could be shut\r\noff at will. No sooner was the staff raised than the aerial vessel\r\nquietly detached itself from the rock to which it had been drawn, and\r\npassed slowly forward in the direction of the mountains. Branchspell\r\nsank below the horizon. The gathering mist blotted out everything\r\noutside a radius of a few miles. The air grew cool and fresh.\r\n\r\nSoon the rock masses ceased on the great, rising plain. Haunte withdrew\r\nthe shutter entirely, and the boat gathered full speed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou say that navigation among the mountains is difficult at night,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nexclaimed Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cI would have thought it impossible.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte grunted. \xe2\x80\x9cYou will have to take risks, and think yourself\r\nfortunate if you come off with nothing worse than a cracked skull. But\r\none thing I can tell you\xe2\x80\x94if you go on disturbing me with your chitchat\r\nwe shan\xe2\x80\x99t get as far as the mountains.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThereafter Maskull was silent.\r\n\r\nThe twilight deepened; the murk grew denser. There was little to look\r\nat, but much to feel. The motion of the boat, which was due to the\r\nnever-ending struggle between the male stones and the force of\r\ngravitation, resembled in an exaggerated fashion the violent tossing of\r\na small craft on a choppy sea. The two passengers became unhappy.\r\nHaunte, from his seat in the stern, gazed at them sardonically with one\r\neye. The darkness now came on rapidly.\r\n\r\nAbout ninety minutes after the commencement of the voyage they arrived\r\nat the foothills of Lichstorm. They began to mount. There was no\r\ndaylight left to see by. Beneath them, however, on both sides of them\r\nand in the rear, the landscape was lighted up for a considerable\r\ndistance by the now vivid blue rays of the twin male stones. Ahead,\r\nwhere these rays did not shine, Haunte was guided by the self-luminous\r\nnature of the rocks, grass, and trees. These were faintly\r\nphosphorescent; the vegetation shone out more strongly than the soil.\r\n\r\nThe moon was not shining and there were no stars; Maskull therefore\r\ninferred that the upper atmosphere was dense with mist. Once or twice,\r\nfrom his sensations of choking, he thought that they were entering a\r\nfogbank, but it was a strange kind of fog, for it had the effect of\r\ndoubling the intensity of every light in front of them. Whenever this\r\nhappened, nightmare feelings attacked him; he experienced transitory,\r\nunreasoning fright and horror.\r\n\r\nNow they passed high above the valley that separated the foothills from\r\nthe mountains themselves. The boat began an ascent of many thousands of\r\nfeet and, as the cliffs were near, Haunte had to manoeuvre carefully\r\nwith the rear light in order to keep clear of them. Maskull watched the\r\ndelicacy of his movements, not without admiration. A long time went by.\r\nIt grew much colder; the air was damp and drafty. The fog began to\r\ndeposit something like snow on their persons. Maskull kept sweating with\r\nterror, not because of the danger they were in, but because of the cloud\r\nbanks that continued to envelop them.\r\n\r\nThey cleared the first line of precipices. Still mounting, but this time\r\nwith a forward motion, as could be seen by the vapours illuminated by\r\nthe male stones through which they passed, they were soon altogether out\r\nof sight of solid ground. Suddenly and quite unexpectedly the moon broke\r\nthrough. In the upper atmosphere thick masses of fog were seen crawling\r\nhither and thither, broken in many places by thin rifts of sky, through\r\none of which Teargeld was shining. Below them, to their left, a gigantic\r\npeak, glittering with green ice, showed itself for a few seconds, and\r\nwas then swallowed up again. All the rest of the world was hidden by the\r\nmist. The moon went in again. Maskull had seen quite enough to make him\r\nlong for the aerial voyage to end.\r\n\r\nThe light from the male stones presently illuminated the face of a new\r\ncliff. It was grand, rugged, and perpendicular. Upward, downward, and on\r\nboth sides, it faded imperceptibly into the night. After coasting it a\r\nlittle way, they observed a shelf of rock jutting out. It was square,\r\nmeasuring about a dozen feet each way. Green snow covered it to a depth\r\nof some inches. Immediately behind it was a dark slit in the rock, which\r\npromised to be the mouth of a cave.\r\n\r\nHaunte skilfully landed the boat on this platform. Standing up, he\r\nraised the staff bearing the keel light and lowered the other; then\r\nremoved both male stones, which he continued to hold in his hand. His\r\nface was thrown into strong relief by the vivid, sparkling blue-white\r\nrays. It looked rather surly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo we get out?\xe2\x80\x9d inquired Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes. I live here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThanks for the successful end of a dangerous journey.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, it has been touch-and-go.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang jumped onto the platform. He was smiling coarsely. \xe2\x80\x9cThere has\r\nbeen no danger, for our destinies lie elsewhere. You are merely a\r\nferryman, Haunte.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs that so?\xe2\x80\x9d returned Haunte, with a most unpleasant laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cI thought\r\nI was carrying men, not gods.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere are we?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull. As he spoke, he got out, but Haunte\r\nremained standing a minute in the boat.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is Sarclash\xe2\x80\x94the second highest mountain in the land.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhich is the highest, then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAdage. Between Sarclash and Adage there is a long ridge\xe2\x80\x94very difficult\r\nin places. About halfway along the ridge, at the lowest point, lies the\r\ntop of the Mornstab Pass, which goes through to Barey. Now you know the\r\nlay of the land.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDoes the woman Sullenbode live near here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNear enough.\xe2\x80\x9d Haunte grinned.\r\n\r\nHe leaped out of the boat and, pushing past the others without ceremony,\r\nwalked straight into the cave.\r\n\r\nMaskull followed, with Corpang at his heels. A few stone steps led to a\r\ndoorway, curtained by the skin of some large beast. Their host pushed\r\nhis way in, never offering to hold the skin aside for them. Maskull made\r\nno comment, but grabbed it with his fist and tugged it away from its\r\nfastenings to the ground. Haunte looked at the skin, and then stared\r\nhard at Maskull with his disagreeable smile, but neither said anything.\r\n\r\nThe place in which they found themselves was a large oblong cavern, with\r\nwalls, floor, and ceiling of natural rock. There were two doorways: that\r\nby which they had entered, and another of smaller size directly\r\nopposite. The cave was cold and cheerless; a damp draft passed from door\r\nto door. Many skins of wild animals lay scattered on the ground. A\r\nnumber of lumps of sun-dried flesh were hanging on a string along the\r\nwall, and a few bulging liquor skins reposed in a corner. There were\r\ntusks, horns, and bones everywhere. Resting against the wall were two\r\nshort hunting spears, having beautiful crystal heads.\r\n\r\nHaunte set down the two male stones on the ground, near the farther\r\ndoor; thire light illuminated the whole cave. He then walked over to the\r\nmeat and, snatching a large piece, began to gnaw it ravenously.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre we invited to the feast?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull.\r\n\r\nHaunte pointed to the hanging flesh and to the liquor skins, but did not\r\npause in his chewing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere\xe2\x80\x99s a cup?\xe2\x80\x9d inquired Maskull, lifting one of the skins.\r\n\r\nHaunte indicated a clay goblet lying on the floor. Maskull picked it up,\r\nundid the neck of the skin, and, resting it under his arm, filled the\r\ncup. Tasting the liquor, he discovered it to be raw spirit. He tossed\r\noff the draught, and then felt much better.\r\n\r\nThe second cupful he proffered to Corpang. The latter took a single sip,\r\nswallowed it, and then passed the cup back without a word. He refused to\r\ndrink again, as long as they were in the cave. Maskull finished the cup,\r\nand began to throw off care.\r\n\r\nGoing to the meat line, he took down a large double handful, and sat\r\ndown on a pile of skins to eat at his ease. The flesh was tough and\r\ncoarse, but he had never tasted anything sweeter. He could not\r\nunderstand the flavour, which was not surprising in a world of strange\r\nanimals. The meal proceeded in silence. Corpang ate sparingly, standing\r\nup, and afterward lay down on a bundle of furs. His bold eyes watched\r\nall the movements of the other two. Haunte had not drunk as yet.\r\n\r\nAt last Maskull concluded his meal. He emptied another cup, sighed\r\npleasantly, and prepared to talk.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow explain further about your women, Haunte.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte fetched another skin of liquor and a second cup. He tore off the\r\nstring with his teeth, and poured out and drank cup after cup in quick\r\nsuccession. Then he sat down, crossed his legs, and turned to Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo they are objectionable?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThey are deadly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDeadly? In what way can they possibly be deadly?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will learn. I was watching you in the boat, Maskull. You had some\r\nbad feelings, eh?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t conceal it. There were times when I felt as if I were\r\nstruggling with a nightmare. What caused it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe female atmosphere of Lichstorm. Sexual passion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI had no passion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat was passion\xe2\x80\x94the first stage. Nature tickles your people into\r\nmarriage, but it tortures us. Wait till you get outside. You\xe2\x80\x99ll have a\r\nreturn of those sensations\xe2\x80\x94only ten times worse. The drink you\xe2\x80\x99ve had\r\nwill see to that.... How do you suppose it will all end?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf I knew, I wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be asking you questions.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte laughed loudly. \xe2\x80\x9cSullenbode.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou mean it will end in my seeking Sullenbode?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what will come of it, Maskull? What will she give you? Sweet,\r\nfainting, white-armed, feminine voluptuousness?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull coolly drank another cup. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd why should she give all that to a\r\npasserby?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, as a matter of fact, she hasn\xe2\x80\x99t it to give. No, what she will\r\ngive you, and what you\xe2\x80\x99ll accept from her, because you can\xe2\x80\x99t help it,\r\nis\xe2\x80\x94anguish, insanity, possibly death.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou may be talking sense, but it sounds like raving to me. Why should I\r\naccept insanity and death?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause your passion will force you to.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat about yourself?\xe2\x80\x9d Maskull asked, biting his nails.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, I have my male stones. I am immune.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs that all that prevents you from being like other men?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, but don\xe2\x80\x99t attempt any tricks, Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull went on drinking steadily, and said nothing for a time. \xe2\x80\x9cSo men\r\nand women here are hostile to each other, and love is unknown?\xe2\x80\x9d he\r\nproceeded at last.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat magic word.... Shall I tell you what love is, Maskull? Love\r\nbetween male and female is impossible. When Maskull loves a woman, it is\r\nMaskull\xe2\x80\x99s female ancestors who are loving her. But here in this land the\r\nmen are pure males. They have drawn nothing from the female side.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere do the male stones come from?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, they are not freaks. There must be whole beds of the stuff\r\nsomewhere. It is all that prevents the world from being a pure female\r\nworld. It would be one big mass of heavy sweetness, without individual\r\nshapes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYet this same sweetness is torturing to men?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe life of an absolute male is fierce. An excess of life is dangerous\r\nto the body. How can it be anything else than torturing?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang now sat up suddenly, and addressed Haunte. \xe2\x80\x9cI remind you of your\r\npromise to tell about Muspel.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte regarded him with a malevolent smile. \xe2\x80\x9cHa! The underground man\r\nhas come to life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, tell us,\xe2\x80\x9d put in Maskull carelessly.\r\n\r\nHaunte drank, and laughed a little. \xe2\x80\x9cWell, the tale\xe2\x80\x99s short, and hardly\r\nworth telling, but since you\xe2\x80\x99re interested.... A stranger came here five\r\nyears ago, inquiring after Muspel-light. His name was Lodd. He came from\r\nthe east. He came up to me one bright morning in summer, outside this\r\nvery cave. If you ask me to describe him\xe2\x80\x94I can\xe2\x80\x99t imagine a second man\r\nlike him. He looked so proud, noble, superior, that I felt my own blood\r\nto be dirty by comparison. You can guess I don\xe2\x80\x99t have this feeling for\r\neveryone. Now that I am recalling him, he was not so much superior as\r\ndifferent. I was so impressed that I rose and talked to him standing. He\r\ninquired the direction of the mountain Adage. He went on to say, \xe2\x80\x98They\r\nsay Muspel-light is sometimes seen there. What do you know of such a\r\nthing?\xe2\x80\x99 I told him the truth\xe2\x80\x94that I knew nothing about it, and then he\r\nwent on, \xe2\x80\x98Well, I am going to Adage. And tell those who come after me on\r\nthe same errand that they had better do the same thing.\xe2\x80\x99 That was the\r\nwhole conversation. He started on his way, and I\xe2\x80\x99ve never seen him or\r\nheard of him since.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo you didn\xe2\x80\x99t have the curiosity to follow him?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, because the moment he had turned his back all my interest in the\r\nman somehow seemed to vanish.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cProbably because he was useless to you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang glanced at Maskull. \xe2\x80\x9cOur road is marked out for us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo it would appear,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull indifferently.\r\n\r\nThe talk flagged for a time. Maskull felt the silence oppressive, and\r\ngrew restless.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you call the colour of your skin, Haunte, as I saw it in\r\ndaylight? It struck me as strange.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDolm,\xe2\x80\x9d said Haunte.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA compound of ulfire and blue,\xe2\x80\x9d explained Corpang.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNow I know. These colours are puzzling for a stranger.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat colours have you in your world?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Corpang.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly three primary ones, but here you seem to have five, though how it\r\ncomes about I can\xe2\x80\x99t imagine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere are two sets of three primary colours here,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang, \xe2\x80\x9cbut\r\nas one of the colours\xe2\x80\x94blue\xe2\x80\x94is identical in both sets, altogether there\r\nare five primary colours.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy two sets?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cProduced by the two suns. Branchspell produces blue, yellow, and red;\r\nAlppain, ulfire, blue, and jale.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s remarkable that explanation has never occurred to me before.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo here you have another illustration of the necessary trinity of\r\nnature. Blue is existence. It is darkness seen through light; a\r\ncontrasting of existence and nothingness. Yellow is relation. In yellow\r\nlight we see the relation of objects in the clearest way. Red is\r\nfeeling. When we see red, we are thrown back on our personal\r\nfeelings.... As regards the Alppain colours, blue stands in the middle\r\nand is therefore not existence, but relation. Ulfire is existence; so it\r\nmust be a different sort of existence.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte yawned. \xe2\x80\x9cThere are marvellous philosophers in your underground\r\nhole.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull got up and looked about him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere does that other door lead to?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBetter explore,\xe2\x80\x9d said Haunte.\r\n\r\nMaskull took him at his word, and strolled across the cave, flinging the\r\ncurtain aside and disappearing into the night. Haunte rose abruptly and\r\nhurried after him.\r\n\r\nCorpang too got to his feet. He went over to the untouched spirit skins,\r\nuntied the necks, and allowed the contents to gush out on to the floor.\r\nNext he took the hunting spears, and snapped off the points between his\r\nhands. Before he had time to resume his seat, Haunte and Maskull\r\nreappeared. The host\xe2\x80\x99s quick, shifty eyes at once took in what had\r\nhappened. He smiled, and turned pale.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou haven\xe2\x80\x99t been idle, friend.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang fixed Haunte with his bold, heavy gaze. \xe2\x80\x9cI thought it well to\r\ndraw your teeth.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull burst out laughing. \xe2\x80\x9cThe toad\xe2\x80\x99s come into the light to some\r\npurpose, Haunte. Who would have expected it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte, after staring hard at Corpang for two or three minutes, suddenly\r\nuttered a strange cry, like an evil spirit, and flung himself upon him.\r\nThe two men began to wrestle like wildcats. They were as often on the\r\nfloor as on their legs, and Maskull could not see who was getting the\r\nbetter of it. He made no attempt to separate them. A thought came into\r\nhis head and, snatching up the two male stones, he ran with them,\r\nlaughing, through the upper doorway, into the open night air.\r\n\r\nThe door overlooked an abyss on another face of the mountain. A narrow\r\nledge, sprinkled with green snow, wound along the cliff to the right; it\r\nwas the only available path. He pitched the pebbles over the edge of the\r\nchasm. Although hard and heavy in his hand, they sank more like feathers\r\nthan stones, and left a long trail of vapour behind. While Maskull was\r\nstill watching them disappear, Haunte came rushing out of the cavern,\r\nfollowed by Corpang. He gripped Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s arm excitedly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat in Krag\xe2\x80\x99s name have you done?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOverboard they have gone,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Maskull, renewing his laughter.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou accursed madman!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte\xe2\x80\x99s luminous colour came and went, just as though his internal\r\nlight were breathing. Then he grew suddenly calm, by a supreme exertion\r\nof his will.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou know this kills me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHaven\xe2\x80\x99t you been doing your best this last hour to make me ripe for\r\nSullenbode? Well then, cheer up, and join the pleasure party!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou say it as a joke, but it is the miserable truth.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte\xe2\x80\x99s jeering malevolence had completely vanished. He looked a sick\r\nman\xe2\x80\x94yet somehow his face had become nobler.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI would be very sorry for you, Haunte, if it did not entail my being\r\nalso very sorry for myself. We are now all three together on the same\r\nerrand\xe2\x80\x94which doesn\xe2\x80\x99t appear to have struck you yet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut why this errand at all?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Corpang quietly. \xe2\x80\x9cCan\xe2\x80\x99t you men\r\nexercise self-control till you have arrived out of danger?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte fixed him with wild eyes. \xe2\x80\x9cNo. The phantoms come trooping in on\r\nme already.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe sat down moodily, but the next minute was up again.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I cannot wait.... the game is started.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSoon afterward, by silent consent, they began to walk the ledge, Haunte\r\nin front. It was narrow, ascending, and slippery, so that extreme\r\ncaution was demanded. The way was lighted by the self-luminous snow and\r\nrocks.\r\n\r\nWhen they had covered about half a mile, Maskull, who went second of the\r\nparty, staggered, caught the cliff, and finally sat down.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe drink works. My old sensations are returning, but worse.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte turned back. \xe2\x80\x9cThen you are a doomed man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull, though fully conscious of his companions and situation,\r\nimagined that he was being oppressed by a black, shapeless, supernatural\r\nbeing, who was trying to clasp him. He was filled with horror, trembled\r\nviolently, yet could not move a limb. Sweat tumbled off his face in\r\ngreat drops. The waking nightmare lasted a long time, but during that\r\nspace it kept coming and going. At one moment the vision seemed on the\r\npoint of departing; the next it almost took shape\xe2\x80\x94which he knew would be\r\nhis death. Suddenly it vanished altogether\xe2\x80\x94he was free. A fresh spring\r\nbreeze fanned his face; he heard the slow, solitary singing of a sweet\r\nbird; and it seemed to him as if a poem had shot together in his soul.\r\nSuch flashing, heartbreaking joy he had never experienced before in all\r\nhis life! Almost immediately that too vanished.\r\n\r\nSitting up, he passed his hand across his eyes and swayed quietly, like\r\none who has been visited by an angel.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour colour changed to white,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat happened?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI passed through torture to love,\xe2\x80\x9d replied Maskull simply.\r\n\r\nHe stood up. Haunte gazed at him sombrely. \xe2\x80\x9cWill you not describe that\r\npassage?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull answered slowly and thoughtfully. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen I was in Matterplay, I\r\nsaw heavy clouds discharge themselves and change to coloured, living\r\nanimals. In the same way, my black, chaotic pangs just now seemed to\r\nconsolidate themselves and spring together as a new sort of joy. The joy\r\nwould not have been possible without the preliminary nightmare. It is\r\nnot accidental; Nature intends it so. The truth has just flashed through\r\nmy brain.... You men of Lichstorm don\xe2\x80\x99t go far enough. You stop at the\r\npangs, without realising that they are birth pangs.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf this is true, you are a great pioneer,\xe2\x80\x9d muttered Haunte.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow does this sensation differ from common love?\xe2\x80\x9d interrogated Corpang.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis was all that love is, multiplied by wildness.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang fingered his chin awhile. \xe2\x80\x9cThe Lichstorm men, however, will\r\nnever reach this stage, for they are too masculine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHaunte turned pale. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy should we alone suffer?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNature is freakish and cruel, and doesn\xe2\x80\x99t act according to justice....\r\nFollow us, Haunte, and escape from it all.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll see,\xe2\x80\x9d muttered Haunte. \xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps I will.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave we far to go, to Sullenbode?\xe2\x80\x9d inquired Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, her home\xe2\x80\x99s under the hanging cap of Sarclash.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is to happen tonight?\xe2\x80\x9d Maskull spoke to himself, but Haunte\r\nanswered him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDon\xe2\x80\x99t expect anything pleasant, in spite of what has just occurred. She\r\nis not a woman, but a mass of pure sex. Your passion will draw her out\r\ninto human shape, but only for a moment. If the change were permanent,\r\nyou would have endowed her with a soul.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps the change might be made permanent.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo do that, it is not enough to desire her; she must desire you as\r\nwell. But why should she desire you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing turns out as one expects,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, shaking his head. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\r\nhad better get on again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey resumed the journey. The ledge still rose, but, on turning a corner\r\nof the cliff, Haunte quitted it and began to climb a steep gully, which\r\nmounted directly to the upper heights. Here they were compelled to use\r\nboth hands and feet. Maskull thought all the while of nothing but the\r\noverwhelming sweetness he had just experienced.\r\n\r\nThe flat ground on top was dry and springy. There was no more snow, and\r\nbright plants appeared. Haunte turned sharply to the left.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis must be under the cap,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is; and within five minutes you will see Sullenbode.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhen he spoke his words, Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s lips surprised him by their tender\r\nsensitiveness. Their action against each other sent thrills throughout\r\nhis body.\r\n\r\nThe grass shone dimly. A huge tree, with glowing branches, came into\r\nsight. It bore a multitude of red fruit, like hanging lanterns, but no\r\nleaves. Underneath this tree Sullenbode was sitting. Her beautiful\r\nlight\xe2\x80\x94a mingling of jale and white\xe2\x80\x94gleamed softly through the darkness.\r\nShe sat erect, on crossed legs, asleep. She was clothed in a singular\r\nskin garment, which started as a cloak thrown over one shoulder, and\r\nended as loose breeches terminating above the knees. Her forearms were\r\nlightly folded, and in one hand she held a half-eaten fruit.\r\n\r\nMaskull stood over her and looked down, deeply interested. He thought he\r\nhad never seen anything half so feminine. Her flesh was almost melting\r\nin its softness. So undeveloped were the facial organs that they looked\r\nscarcely human; only the lips were full, pouting, and expressive. In\r\ntheir richness, these lips seemed like a splash of vivid will on a\r\nbackground of slumbering protoplasm. Her hair was undressed. Its colour\r\ncould not be distinguished. It was long and tangled, and had been tucked\r\ninto her garment behind, for convenience.\r\n\r\nCorpang looked calm and sullen, but both the others were visibly\r\nagitated. Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s heart was hammering away under his chest. Haunte\r\npulled him, and said, \xe2\x80\x9cMy head feels as if it were being torn from my\r\nshoulders.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat can that mean?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYet there\xe2\x80\x99s a horrible joy in it,\xe2\x80\x9d added Haunte, with a sickly smile.\r\n\r\nHe put his hand on the woman\xe2\x80\x99s shoulder. She awoke softly, glanced up at\r\nthem, smiled, and then resumed eating her fruit. Maskull did not imagine\r\nthat she had intelligence enough to speak. Haunte suddenly dropped on\r\nhis knees, and kissed her lips.\r\n\r\nShe did not repulse him. During the continuance of the kiss, Maskull\r\nnoticed with a shock that her face was altering. The features emerged\r\nfrom their indistinctness and became human, and almost powerful. The\r\nsmile faded, a scowl took its place. She thrust Haunte away, rose to her\r\nfeet, and stared beneath bent brows at the three men, each one in turn.\r\nMaskull came last; his face she studied for quite a long time, but\r\nnothing indicated what she thought.\r\n\r\nMeanwhile Haunte again approached her, staggering and grinning. She\r\nsuffered him quietly; but the instant lips met lips the second time, he\r\nfell backward with a startled cry, as though he had come in contact with\r\nan electric wire. The back of his head struck the ground, and he lay\r\nthere motionless.\r\n\r\nCorpang sprang forward to his assistance. But, when he saw what had\r\nhappened, he left him where he was.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMaskull, come here quickly!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe light was perceptibly fading from Haunte\xe2\x80\x99s skin, as Maskull bent\r\nover. The man was dead. His face was unrecognisable. The head had been\r\nsplit from the top downward into two halves, streaming with strange-\r\ncoloured blood, as though it had received a terrible blow from an axe.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis couldn\xe2\x80\x99t be from the fall,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, Sullenbode did it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull turned quickly to look at the woman. She had resumed her former\r\nattitude on the ground. The momentary intelligence had vanished from her\r\nface, and she was again smiling.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nChapter 19. SULLENBODE\r\n\r\nSullenbode\xe2\x80\x99s naked skin glowed softly through the darkness, but the\r\nclothed part of her person was invisible. Maskull watched her senseless,\r\nsmiling face, and shivered. Strange feelings ran through his body.\r\n\r\nCorpang spoke out of the night. \xe2\x80\x9cShe looks like an evil spirit filled\r\nwith deadliness.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt was like deliberately kissing lightning.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHaunte was insane with passion.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo am I,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull quietly. \xe2\x80\x9cMy body seems full of rocks, all\r\ngrinding against one another.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is what I was afraid of.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt appears I shall have to kiss her too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang pulled his arm. \xe2\x80\x9cHave you lost all manliness?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBut Maskull impatiently shook himself free. He plucked nervously at his\r\nbeard, and stared at Sullenbode. His lips kept twitching. After this had\r\ngone on for a few minutes, he stepped forward, bent over the woman, and\r\nlifted her bodily in his arms. Setting her upright against the rugged\r\ntree trunk, he kissed her.\r\n\r\nA cold, knifelike shock passed down his frame. He thought that it was\r\ndeath, and lost consciousness.\r\n\r\nWhen his sense returned, Sullenbode was holding him by the shoulder with\r\none hand at arm\xe2\x80\x99s length, searching his face with gloomy eyes. At first\r\nhe failed to recognise her; it was not the woman he had kissed, but\r\nanother. Then he gradually realised that her face was identical with\r\nthat which Haunte\xe2\x80\x99s action had called into existence. A great calmness\r\ncame upon him; his bad sensations had disappeared.\r\n\r\nSullenbode was transformed into a living soul. Her skin was firm, her\r\nfeatures were strong, her eyes gleamed with the consciousness of power.\r\nShe was tall and slight, but slow in all her gestures and movements. Her\r\nface was not beautiful. It was long, and palely lighted, while the mouth\r\ncrossed the lower half like a gash of fire. The lips were as voluptuous\r\nas before. Her brows were heavy. There was nothing vulgar in her\xe2\x80\x94she\r\nlooked the kingliest of all women. She appeared not more than twenty-\r\nfive.\r\n\r\nGrowing tired, apparently, of his scrutiny, she pushed him a little way\r\nand allowed her arm to drop, at the same time curving her mouth into a\r\nlong, bowlike smile. \xe2\x80\x9cWhom have I to thank for this gift of life?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHer voice was rich, slow, and odd. Maskull felt himself in a dream.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy name is Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe motioned to him to come a step nearer. \xe2\x80\x9cListen, Maskull. Man after\r\nman has drawn me into the world, but they could not keep me there, for I\r\ndid not wish it. But now you have drawn me into it for all time, for\r\ngood or evil.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull stretched a hand toward the now invisible corpse, and said\r\nquietly, \xe2\x80\x9cWhat have you to say about him?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho was it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHaunte.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo that was Haunte. The news will travel far and wide. He was a famous\r\nman.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a horrible affair. I can\xe2\x80\x99t think that you killed him\r\ndeliberately.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe women are endowed with terrible power, but it is our only\r\nprotection. We do not want these visits; we loathe them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI might have died, too.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou came together?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere were three of us. Corpang still stands over there.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI see a faintly glimmering form. What do you want of me, Corpang?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen go away, and leave me with Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo need, Corpang. I am coming with you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is not that pleasure, then?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded the low, earnest voice, out\r\nof the darkness.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, that pleasure has not returned.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode gripped his arm hard. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat pleasure are you speaking of?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA presentiment of love, which I felt not long ago.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what do you feel now?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCalm and free.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode\xe2\x80\x99s face seemed like a pallid mask, hiding a slow, swelling sea\r\nof elemental passions. \xe2\x80\x9cI do not know how it will end, Maskull, but we\r\nwill still keep together a little. Where are you going?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo Adage,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang, stepping forward.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut why?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are following the steps of Lodd, who went there years ago, to find\r\nMuspel-light.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat light is that?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s the light of another world.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe quest is grand. But cannot women see that light?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn one condition,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang. \xe2\x80\x9cThey must forget their sex. Womanhood\r\nand love belong to life, while Muspel is above life.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI give you all other men,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sullenbode. \xe2\x80\x9cMaskull is mine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo. I am not here to help Maskull to a lover but to remind him of the\r\nexistence of nobler things.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are a good man. But you two alone will never strike the road to\r\nAdage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you acquainted with it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAgain the woman gripped Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s arm. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat is love\xe2\x80\x94which Corpang\r\ndespises?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull looked at her attentively. Sullenbode went on, \xe2\x80\x9cLove is that\r\nwhich is perfectly willing to disappear and become nothing, for the sake\r\nof the beloved.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang wrinkled his forehead. \xe2\x80\x9cA magnanimous female lover is new in my\r\nexperience.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull put him aside with his hand, and said to Sullenbode, \xe2\x80\x9cAre you\r\ncontemplating a sacrifice?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe gazed at her feet, and smiled. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat does it matter what my thoughts\r\nare? Tell me, are you starting at once, or do you mean to rest first?\r\nIt\xe2\x80\x99s a rough road to Adage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s in your mind?\xe2\x80\x9d demanded Maskull.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI will guide you a little. When we reach the ridge between Sarclash and\r\nAdage, perhaps I shall turn back.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen if the moon shines perhaps you will arrive before daybreak, but if\r\nit is dark it\xe2\x80\x99s hardly likely.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s not what I meant. What will become of you after we have parted\r\ncompany?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall return somewhere\xe2\x80\x94perhaps here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull went close up to her, in order to study her face better. \xe2\x80\x9cShall\r\nyou sink back into\xe2\x80\x94the old state?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, Maskull, thank heaven.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen how will you live?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode calmly removed the hand which he had placed on her arm. There\r\nwas a sort of swirling flame in her eyes. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd who said I would go on\r\nliving?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull blinked at her in bewilderment. A few moments passed before he\r\nspoke again. \xe2\x80\x9cYou women are a sacrificing lot. You know I can\xe2\x80\x99t leave\r\nyou like this.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTheir eyes met. Neither withdrew them, and neither felt embarrassed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will always be the most generous of men, Maskull. Now let us go....\r\nCorpang is a single-minded personage, and the least we others\xe2\x80\x94who aren\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nso single-minded\xe2\x80\x94can do is to help him to his destination. We mustn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\ninquire whether the destination of single-minded men is as a rule worth\r\narriving at.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf it is good for Maskull, it will be good for me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, no vessel can hold more than its appointed measure.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang gave a wry smile. \xe2\x80\x9cDuring your long sleep you appear to have\r\npicked up wisdom.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, Corpang, I have met many men, and explored many minds.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAs they moved off, Maskull remembered Haunte.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCan we not bury that poor fellow?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBy this time tomorrow we shall need burial ourselves. But I do not\r\ninclude Corpang.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have no tools, so you must have your way. You killed him, but I am\r\nthe real murderer. I stole his protecting light.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSurely that death is balanced by the life you have given me.\xe2\x80\x9d They left\r\nthe spot in the direction opposite to that by which the three men had\r\narrived. After a few steps, they came to green snow again. At the same\r\ntime the flat ground ended, and they started to traverse a steep,\r\npathless mountain slope. The snow and rocks glimmered, their own bodies\r\nshone; otherwise everything was dark. The mists swirled around them, but\r\nMaskull had no more nightmares. The breeze was cold, pure, and steady.\r\nThey walked in file, Sullenbode leading; her movements were slow and\r\nfascinating. Corpang came last. His stern eyes saw nothing ahead but an\r\nalluring girl and a half-infatuated man.\r\n\r\nFor a long time they continued crossing the rough and rocky slope,\r\nmaintaining a slightly upward course. The angle was so steep that a\r\nfalse step would have been fatal. The high ground was on their right.\r\nAfter a while, the hillside on the left hand changed to level ground,\r\nand they seemed to have joined another spur of the mountain. The\r\nascending slope on the right hand persisted for a few hundred yards\r\nmore. Then Sullenbode bore sharply to the left, and they found level\r\nground all around them.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are on the ridge,\xe2\x80\x9d announced the woman, halting.\r\n\r\nThe others came up to her, and at the same instant the moon burst\r\nthrough the clouds, illuminating the whole scene.\r\n\r\nMaskull uttered a cry. The wild, noble, lonely beauty of the view was\r\nquite unexpected. Teargeld was high in the sky to their left, shining\r\ndown on them from behind. Straight in front, like an enormously wide,\r\nsmoothly descending road, lay the great ridge which went on to Adage,\r\nthough Adage itself was out of sight. It was never less than two hundred\r\nyards wide. It was covered with green snow, in some places entirely, but\r\nin other places the naked rocks showed through like black teeth. From\r\nwhere they stood they were unable to see the sides of the ridge, or what\r\nlay underneath. On the right hand, which was north, the landscape was\r\nblurred and indistinct. There were no peaks there; it was the distant,\r\nlow-lying land of Barey. But on the left hand appeared a whole forest of\r\nmighty pinnacles, near and far, as far as the eye could see in\r\nmoonlight. All glittered green, and all possessed the extraordinary\r\nhanging caps that characterised the Lichstorm range. These caps were of\r\nfantastic shapes, and each one was different. The valley directly\r\nopposite them was filled with rolling mist.\r\n\r\nSarclash was a mighty mountain mass in the shape of a horseshoe. Its two\r\nends pointed west, and were separated from each other by a mile or more\r\nof empty space. The northern end became the ridge on which they stood.\r\nThe southern end was the long line of cliffs on that part of the\r\nmountain where Haunte\xe2\x80\x99s cave was situated. The connecting curve was the\r\nsteep slope they had just traversed. One peak of Sarclash was invisible.\r\n\r\nIn the south-west many mountains raised their heads. In addition, a few\r\nsummits, which must have been of extraordinary height, appeared over the\r\nsouth side of the horseshoe.\r\n\r\nMaskull turned round to put a question to Sullenbode, but when he saw\r\nher for the first time in moonlight the words he had framed died on his\r\nlips. The gashlike mouth no longer dominated her other features, and the\r\nface, pale as ivory and most femininely shaped, suddenly became almost\r\nbeautiful. The lips were a long, womanish curve of rose-red. Her hair\r\nwas a dark maroon. Maskull was greatly disturbed; he thought that she\r\nresembled a spirit, rather than a woman.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat puzzles you?\xe2\x80\x9d she asked, smiling.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing. But I would like to see you by sunlight.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps you never will.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour life must be most solitary.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe explored his features with her black, slow-gleaming eyes. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy do\r\nyou fear to speak your feelings, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThings seem to open up before me like a sunrise, but what it means I\r\ncan\xe2\x80\x99t say.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode laughed outright. \xe2\x80\x9cIt assuredly does not mean the approach of\r\nnight.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang, who had been staring steadily along the ridge, here abruptly\r\nbroke in. \xe2\x80\x9cThe road is plain now, Maskull. If you wish it, I\xe2\x80\x99ll go on\r\nalone.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, we\xe2\x80\x99ll go on together. Sullenbode will accompany us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA little way,\xe2\x80\x9d said the woman, \xe2\x80\x9cbut not to Adage, to pit my strength\r\nagainst unseen powers. That light is not for me. I know how to renounce\r\nlove, but I will never be a traitor to it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho knows what we shall find on Adage, or what will happen? Corpang is\r\nas ignorant as myself.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nCorpang looked him full in the face. \xe2\x80\x9cMaskull, you are quite well aware\r\nthat you never dare approach that awful fire in the society of a\r\nbeautiful woman.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull gave an uneasy laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat Corpang doesn\xe2\x80\x99t tell you,\r\nSullenbode, is that I am far better acquainted with Muspel-light than\r\nhe, and that, but for a chance meeting with me, he would still be saying\r\nhis prayers in Threal.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStill, what he says must be true,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, looking from one to the\r\nother.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd so I am not to be allowed to\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo long as I am with you, I shall urge you onward, and not backward,\r\nMaskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe need not quarrel yet,\xe2\x80\x9d he remarked, with a forced smile. \xe2\x80\x9cNo doubt\r\nthings will straighten themselves out.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode began kicking the snow about with her foot. \xe2\x80\x9cI picked up\r\nanother piece of wisdom in my sleep, Corpang.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTell it to me, then.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMen who live by laws and rules are parasites. Others shed their\r\nstrength to bring these laws out of nothing into the light of day, but\r\nthe law-abiders live at their ease\xe2\x80\x94they have conquered nothing for\r\nthemselves.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is given to some to discover, and to others to preserve and perfect.\r\nYou cannot condemn me for wishing Maskull well.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, but a child cannot lead a thunderstorm.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey started walking again along the centre of the ridge. All three were\r\nabreast, Sullenbode in the middle.\r\n\r\nThe road descended by an easy gradient, and was for a long distance\r\ncomparatively smooth. The freezing point seemed higher than on Earth,\r\nfor the few inches of snow through which they trudged felt almost warm\r\nto their naked feet. Maskull\xe2\x80\x99s soles were by now like tough hides. The\r\nmoonlit snow was green and dazzling. Their slanting, abbreviated shadows\r\nwere sharply defined, and red-black in colour. Maskull, who walked on\r\nSullenbode\xe2\x80\x99s right hand, looked constantly to the left, toward the\r\ngalaxy of glorious distant peaks.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou cannot belong to this world,\xe2\x80\x9d said the woman. \xe2\x80\x9cMen of your stamp\r\nare not to be looked for here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I have come here from Earth.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs that larger than our world?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSmaller, I think. Small, and overcrowded with men and women. With all\r\nthose people, confusion would result but for orderly laws, and therefore\r\nthe laws are of iron. As adventure would be impossible without\r\nencroaching on these laws, there is no longer any spirit of adventure\r\namong the Earthmen. Everything is safe, vulgar, and completed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo men hate women there, and women men?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, the meeting of the sexes is sweet, though shameful. So poignant is\r\nthe sweetness that the accompanying shame is ignored, with open eyes.\r\nThere is no hatred, or only among a few eccentric persons.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat shame surely must be the rudiment of our Lichstorm passion. But\r\nnow say\xe2\x80\x94why did you come here?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo meet with new experiences, perhaps. The old ones no longer\r\ninterested me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow long have you been in this world?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the end of my fourth day.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen tell me what you have seen and done during those four days. You\r\ncannot have been inactive.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGreat misfortunes have happened to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe proceeded briefly to relate everything that had taken place from the\r\nmoment of his first awakening in the scarlet desert. Sullenbode\r\nlistened, with half-closed eyes, nodding her head from time to time.\r\nOnly twice did she interrupt him. After his description of Tydomin\xe2\x80\x99s\r\ndeath, she said, speaking in a low voice\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cNone of us women ought by\r\nright of nature to fall short of Tydomin in sacrifice. For that one act\r\nof hers, I almost love her, although she brought evil to your door.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nAgain, speaking of Gleameil, she remarked, \xe2\x80\x9cThat grand-souled girl I\r\nadmire the most of all. She listened to her inner voice, and to nothing\r\nelse besides. Which of us others is strong enough for that?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nWhen his tale was quite over, Sullenbode said, \xe2\x80\x9cDoes it not strike you,\r\nMaskull, that these women you have met have been far nobler than the\r\nmen?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI recognise that. We men often sacrifice ourselves, but only for a\r\nsubstantial cause. For you women almost any cause will serve. You love\r\nthe sacrifice for its own sake, and that is because you are naturally\r\nnoble.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nTurning her head a little, she threw him a smile so proud, yet so sweet,\r\nthat he was struck into silence.\r\n\r\nThey tramped on quietly for some distance, and then he said, \xe2\x80\x9cNow you\r\nunderstand the sort of man I am. Much brutality, more weakness, scant\r\npity for anyone\xe2\x80\x94Oh, it has been a bloody journey!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe laid her hand on his arm. \xe2\x80\x9cI, for one, would not have it less\r\nrugged.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing good can be said of my crimes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo me you seem like a lonely giant, searching for you know not what....\r\nThe grandest that life holds.... You at least have no cause to look up\r\nto women.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThanks, Sullenbode!\xe2\x80\x9d he responded, with a troubled smile.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhen Maskull passes, let people watch. Everyone is thrown out of your\r\nroad. You go on, looking neither to right nor left.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTake care that you are not thrown as well,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang gravely.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMaskull shall do with me whatever he pleases, old skull! And for\r\nwhatever he does, I will thank him.... In place of a heart you have a\r\nbag of loose dust. Someone has described love to you. You have had it\r\ndescribed to you. You have heard that it is a small, fearful, selfish\r\njoy. It is not that\xe2\x80\x94it is wild, and scornful, and sportive, and\r\nbloody.... How should you know.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSelfishness has far too many disguises.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf a woman wills to give up all, what can there be selfish in that?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly do not deceive yourself. Act decisively, or fate will be too swift\r\nfor you both.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSullenbode studied him through her lashes. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you mean death\xe2\x80\x94his death\r\nas well as mine?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou go too far, Corpang,\xe2\x80\x9d said Maskull, turning a shade darker. \xe2\x80\x9cI\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t accept you as the arbiter of our fortunes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf honest counsel is disagreeable to you, let me go on ahead.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe woman detained him with her slow, light fingers. \xe2\x80\x9cI wish you to stay\r\nwith us.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI think you may know what you are talking about. I don\xe2\x80\x99t wish to bring\r\nharm to Maskull. Presently I\xe2\x80\x99ll leave you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat will be best,\xe2\x80\x9d said Corpang.\r\n\r\nMaskull looked angry. \xe2\x80\x9cI shall decide\xe2\x80\x94Sullenbode, whether you go on, or\r\nback, I stay with you. My mind is made up.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAn expression of joyousness overspread her face, in spite of her efforts\r\nto conceal it. \xe2\x80\x9cWhy do you scowl at me, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe returned no answer, but continued walking onward with puckered brows.\r\nAfter a dozen paces or so, he halted abruptly. \xe2\x80\x9cWait, Sullenbode!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe others came to a standstill. Corpang looked puzzled, but the woman\r\nsmiled. Maskull, without a word, bent over and kissed her lips. Then he\r\nrelinquished her body, and turned around to Corpang.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow do you, in your great wisdom, interpret that kiss?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt requires no great wisdom to interpret kisses, Maskull.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHereafter, never dare to come between us. Sullenbode belongs to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThen I say no more; but you are a fated man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nFrom that time forward he spoke not another word to either of the\r\nothers.\r\n\r\nA heavy gleam appeared in the woman\xe2\x80\x99s eyes. \xe2\x80\x9cNow things are changed,\r\nMaskull. Where are you taking me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cChoose, you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe man I love must complete his journey. I won\xe2\x80\x99t have it otherwise.\r\nYou shall not stand lower than Corpang.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere you go, I will go.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd I\xe2\x80\x94as long as your love endures, I will accompany you\xe2\x80\x94even to\r\nAdage.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you doubt its lasting?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wish not to.... Now I will tell you what I refused to tell you\r\nbefore. The term of your love is the term of my life. When you love me\r\nno longer, I must die.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd why?\xe2\x80\x9d asked Maskull slowly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, that\xe2\x80\x99s the responsibility you incurred when you kissed me for the\r\nfirst time. I never meant to tell you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you mean that if I had gone on alone, you would have died?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have no other life but what you give me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe gazed at her mournfully, without attempting to reply, and then slowly\r\nplaced his arms around her body. During this embrace he turned very\r\npale, but Sullenbode grew as white as chalk.\r\n\r\nA few minutes later the journey toward Adage was resumed.\r\n\r\nThey had been walking for two hours. Teargeld was higher in the sky and\r\nnearer the south. They had descended many hundred feet, and the\r\ncharacter of the ridge began to alter for the worse. The thin snow\r\ndisappeared, and gave way to moist, boggy ground. It was all little\r\ngrassy hillocks and marshes. They began to slip about and become\r\ndraggled with mud. Conversation ceased; Sullenbode led the way, and the\r\nmen followed in her tracks. The southern half of the landscape grew\r\ngrander. The greenish light of the brilliant moon, shining on the\r\nmultitude of snow-green peaks, caused it to appear like a spectral\r\nworld. Their nearest neighbour towered high above them on the other side\r\nof the valley, due south, some five miles distant. It was a slender,\r\ninaccessible, dizzy spire of black rock, the angles of which were too\r\nsteep to retain snow. A great upward-curving horn of rock sprang out\r\nfrom its topmost pinnacle. For a long time it constituted their cheif\r\nlandmark.\r\n\r\nThe whole ridge gradually became saturated with moisture. The surface\r\nsoil was spongy, and rested on impermeable rock; it breathed in the damp\r\nmists by night, and breathed them out again by day, under Branchspell\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nrays. The walking grew first unpleasant, then difficult, and finally\r\ndangerous. None of the party could distinguish firm ground from bog.\r\nSullenbode sank up to her waist in a pit of slime; Maskull rescued her,\r\nbut after this incident took the lead himself. Corpang was the next to\r\nmeet with trouble. Exploring a new path for himself, he tumbled into\r\nliquid mud up to his shoulders, and narrowly escaped a filthy death.\r\nAfter Maskull had got him out, at great personal risk, they proceeded\r\nonce more; but now the scramble changed from bad to worse. Each step had\r\nto be thoroughly tested before weight was put upon it, and even so the\r\ntest frequently failed. All of them went in so often, that in the end\r\nthey no longer resembled human beings, but walking pillars plastered\r\nfrom top to toe with black filth. The hardest work fell to Maskull. He\r\nnot only had the exhausting task of beating the way, but was continually\r\ncalled upon to help his companions out of their difficulties. Without\r\nhim they could not have got through.\r\n\r\nAfter a peculiarly evil patch, they paused to recruit their strength.\r\nCorpang\xe2\x80\x99s breathing was difficult, Sullenbode was quiet, listless, and\r\ndepressed.\r\n\r\nMaskull gazed at them doubtfully. \xe2\x80\x9cDoes this continue?\xe2\x80\x9d he inquired.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo. I think,\xe2\x80\x9d replied the woman, \xe2\x80\x9cwe can\xe2\x80\x99t be far from the Mornstab\r\nPass. After that we shall begin to climb again, and then the road will\r\nimprove perhaps.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCan you have been here before?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnce I have been to the Pass, but it was not so bad then.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are tired out, Sullenbode.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat of it?\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, smiling faintly. \xe2\x80\x9cWhen one has a terrible\r\nlover, one must pay the price.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe cannot get there tonight, so let us stop at the first shelter we\r\ncome to.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI leave it to you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe paced up and down, while the others sat. \xe2\x80\x9cDo you regret anything?\xe2\x80\x9d he\r\ndemanded suddenly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, Maskull, nothing. I regret nothing.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYour feelings are unchanged?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLove can\xe2\x80\x99t go back\xe2\x80\x94it can only go on.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, eternally on. It is so.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, I don\xe2\x80\x99t mean that. There is a climax, but when the climax has been\r\nreached, love if it still wants to ascend must turn to sacrifice.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s a dreadful creed,\xe2\x80\x9d he said in a low voice, turning pale beneath\r\nhis coating of mud.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps my nature is discordant.... I am tired. I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what I\r\nfeel.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIn a few minutes they were on their feet again, and the journey\r\nrecommenced. Within half an hour they had reached the Mornstab Pass.\r\n\r\nThe ground here was drier; the broken land to the north served to drain\r\noff the moisture of the soil. Sullenbode led them to the northern edge\r\nof the ridge, to show them the nature of the country. The pass was\r\nnothing but a gigantic landslip on both sides of the ridge, where it was\r\nthe lowest above the underlying land. A series of huge broken terraces\r\nof earth and rock descended toward Barey. They were overgrown with\r\nstunted vegetation. It was quite possible to get down to the lowlands\r\nthat way, but rather difficult. On either side of the landslip, to east\r\nand west, the ridge came down in a long line of sheer, terrific cliffs.\r\nA low haze concealed Barey from view. Complete stillness was in the air,\r\nbroken only by the distant thundering of an invisible waterfall.\r\n\r\nMaskull and Sullenbode sat down on a boulder, facing the open country.\r\nThe moon was directly behind them, high up. It was almost as light as an\r\nEarth day.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTonight is like life,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sullenbode.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow so?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo lovely above and around us, so foul underfoot.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull sighed. \xe2\x80\x9cPoor girl, you are unhappy.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd you\xe2\x80\x94are you happy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe thought a while, and then replied\xe2\x80\x94\xe2\x80\x9cNo. No, I\xe2\x80\x99m not happy. Love is not\r\nhappiness.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is it, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRestlessness\xe2\x80\x94unshed tears\xe2\x80\x94thoughts too grand for our soul to think...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sullenbode.\r\n\r\nAfter a time she asked, \xe2\x80\x9cWhy were we created, just to live for a few\r\nyears and then disappear?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are told that we shall live again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, Maskull?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps in Muspel,\xe2\x80\x9d he added thoughtfully.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat kind of life will that be?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSurely we shall meet again. Love is too wonderful and mysterious a\r\nthing to remain uncompleted.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe gave a slight shiver, and turned away from him. \xe2\x80\x9cThis dream is\r\nuntrue. Love is completed here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow can that be, when sooner or later it is brutally interrupted by\r\nFate?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is completed by anguish.... Oh, why must it always be enjoyment for\r\nus? Can\xe2\x80\x99t we suffer\xe2\x80\x94can\xe2\x80\x99t we go on suffering, forever and ever? Maskull,\r\nuntil love crushes our spirit, finally and without remedy, we don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nbegin to feel ourselves.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull gazed at her with a troubled expression. \xe2\x80\x9cCan the memory of love\r\nbe worth more than its presence and reality?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou don\xe2\x80\x99t understand. Those pangs are more precious than all the rest\r\nbeside.\xe2\x80\x9d She caught at him. \xe2\x80\x9cOh, if you could only see inside my mind,\r\nMaskull! You would see strange things.... I can\xe2\x80\x99t explain. It is all\r\nconfused, even to myself.... This love is quite different from what I\r\nthought.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe sighed again. \xe2\x80\x9cLove is a strong drink. Perhaps it is too strong for\r\nhuman beings. And I think that it overturns our reason in different\r\nways.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThey remained sitting side by side, staring straight before them with\r\nunseeing eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt doesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter,\xe2\x80\x9d said Sullenbode at last, with a smile, getting up.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSoon it will be ended, one way or another. Come, let us be off!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nMaskull too got up.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere\xe2\x80\x99s Corpang?\xe2\x80\x9d he asked listlessly.\r\n\r\nThey both looked across the ridge in the direction of Adage. At the\r\npoint where they stood it was nearly a mile wide. It sloped perceptibly\r\ntoward the southern edge, giving all the earth the appearance of a heavy\r\nlist. Toward the west the ground continued level for a thousand yards,\r\nbut then a high, sloping, grassy hill went right across the ridge from\r\nside to side, like a vast billow on the verge of breaking. It shut out\r\nall further view beyond.
